2026-03-13 AI计算规模化发展的最大瓶颈 Dylan Patel — The single biggest bottleneck to scaling AI compute 
Info
Podcast: Dwarkesh Patel
Episode: Dylan Patel — The single biggest bottleneck to scaling AI compute
Link: https://app.podwise.ai/dashboard/episodes/7521578
Publish Time: 2026-03-13
Save Time: 2026-05-24
Summary
The podcast explores the future of AI compute, particularly focusing on potential bottlenecks and the evolving strategies of major players like OpenAI, Anthropic, and Google. Dylan Patel of SemiAnalysis provides insights into hyperscaler CapEx timelines, the competitive dynamics of compute acquisition, and the increasing value of GPUs as models improve. The conversation highlights how memory constraints and the limitations of EUV lithography tools could shape AI development, with potential shifts in market dominance between the West and China. It also touches on alternative energy sources for data centers and the feasibility of space-based compute, questioning long-held assumptions in the AI industry.
本播客探讨了人工智能计算的未来，特别关注潜在的瓶颈以及 OpenAI、Anthropic 和谷歌等主要参与者不断演变的战略。SemiAnalysis 的 Dylan Patel 深入分析了超大规模企业资本支出时间表、计算资源获取的竞争动态以及随着模型改进，GPU 日益增长的价值。对话强调了内存限制和 EUV 光刻工具的局限性如何塑造人工智能的发展，以及西方和中国之间潜在的市场主导地位转变。它还涉及数据中心的替代能源和天基计算的可行性，质疑人工智能行业长期以来的假设。
Takeaways
The most significant bottleneck to AI development by 2030 will be the production capacity of semiconductor manufacturing tools, specifically EUV machines, limiting the overall gigawatts of AI compute deployable.
到 2030 年，人工智能发展最显著的瓶颈将是半导体制造工具的产能，特别是 EUV 光刻机，这将限制可部署的人工智能计算总千兆瓦数。
Anthropic's initial conservative approach to compute acquisition has put them at a disadvantage compared to OpenAI, forcing them to pay premium prices and use lower-quality providers to meet unexpected revenue growth.
与 OpenAI 相比，Anthropic 最初在计算资源采购方面采取的保守策略使其处于劣势，迫使其支付高溢价并使用质量较低的供应商，以满足意外的收入增长。
The value of GPUs can increase over time as models improve, allowing them to process more valuable tokens, thus challenging the traditional depreciation cycle assumptions.
随着模型的改进，GPU 的价值会随着时间的推移而增加，从而使它们能够处理更有价值的 token，从而挑战传统的折旧周期假设。
NVIDIA strategically fractures complementary industries like NeoClouds and data providers to maintain leverage and maximize its position in the AI ecosystem.
英伟达有策略地分化 NeoClouds 和数据提供商等互补产业，以保持影响力并最大限度地提高其在人工智能生态系统中的地位。
The increasing cost of memory, driven by AI demand, will negatively impact consumer electronics, potentially leading to reduced smartphone volumes and consumer resentment towards AI.
人工智能需求驱动的内存成本上涨将对消费电子产品产生负面影响，可能导致智能手机销量下降和消费者对人工智能的反感。
Google's initial misjudgment in compute procurement led to Anthropic leveraging Google's TPUs before Google fully recognized the potential revenue inflection.
谷歌最初在计算资源采购方面的误判导致 Anthropic 在谷歌完全意识到潜在收入增长之前利用了谷歌的 TPU。
A significant portion of hyperscalers' CapEx is spent on long-term infrastructure investments, such as turbine deposits and data center construction, for compute capacity that will come online years into the future.
超大规模企业的大部分资本支出用于长期基础设施投资，例如涡轮机押金和数据中心建设，这些计算能力将在未来几年内上线。
The modularization of data centers and the prefabrication of components in factories are crucial for overcoming labor constraints in the rapid scaling of AI compute infrastructure.
数据中心的模块化和工厂中组件的预制对于克服人工智能计算基础设施快速扩展中的劳动力限制至关重要。
Q & A
Q: What is the concrete advantage that OpenAI has gotten if they end up at similar compute numbers by 2027; is it just that they’re going to end this year with different gigawatts, and if so, how many gigawatts is Anthropic and OpenAI going to have by the end of this year?
Q: 如果到 2027 年，OpenAI 的算力最终达到相似的水平，那么他们获得的具体优势是什么？仅仅是因为他们今年年底的千兆瓦数不同吗？如果是这样，到今年年底，Anthropic 和 OpenAI 将拥有多少千兆瓦？
A: To acquire XS Compute, there is capacity at hyperscalers, and not all contracts for compute are long term, five years. There's compute that in 2023 or 2024, H100, 2025, that were signed at not five-year deals. OpenAI, the vast majority of their compute is signed at five-year deals. There were many other customers that had one-year, two-year, three-year deals, six-month deals on demand. As these contracts roll off, who is the participant in the market most willing to pay price? In this sense, we've seen H100 prices inflect a lot and go up, and people willing to sign long-term deals for above  2.40 for two to three years for H100s, which if you think about the margin,  2.40, those margins are way higher. Anthropic I think we'll be able to get to like five gigawatts-ish, maybe a little bit more by the end of the year, through themselves as well as their product being served through Bedrock or through Vertex or through Foundry. I think they'll be able to get to five or six gigawatts, which is way above their initial plans. And anyways, that's sort of like, and OpenAI will be roughly the same, maybe a little higher, actually a little bit higher based on our numbers.
A: 为了获得 XS 算力，超大规模企业是有产能的，而且并非所有算力合同都是长期的，五年。在 2023 年或 2024 年，H100，2025 年，有些合同并不是五年期的。OpenAI，他们绝大多数的算力都是五年期的合同。还有许多其他客户签订了一年、两年、三年，甚至六个月的按需合同。当这些合同到期时，谁是市场上最愿意支付价格的参与者？从这个意义上说，我们已经看到 H100 的价格发生了很大的变化并上涨，甚至有人愿意签订长期合同，价格高于 2 美元。我见过一些人工智能实验室签订的合同，H100 的价格高达 2.40 美元，为期两到三年，如果你考虑利润，Hopper 的利润是 1.40 美元，当你发布 Hopper 或在五年内构建它，而现在你签订的合同是两到三年，价格是 2.40 美元，那么利润率要高得多。我认为 Anthropic 到今年年底将能够达到大约 5 千兆瓦左右，甚至更多一点，通过他们自己以及他们的产品通过 Bedrock 或通过 Vertex 或通过 Foundry 提供服务。我认为他们将能够达到 5 到 6 千兆瓦，这远高于他们最初的计划。无论如何，这有点像，OpenAI 大致相同，可能略高，实际上根据我们的数字，会略高一些。

Q: If Anthropic was not on track to have 5 gigawatts by the end of this year, but it needs that to serve both the revenue that's gone crazier than expected, and maybe it's going to be even more than that, plus the research and training to make sure its models are good enough for next year, how, how, where is that going to come from?
Q: 如果 Anthropic 到今年年底没有达到 5 千兆瓦的目标，但它需要这些算力来满足收入（收入增长超出预期，甚至可能更高），以及研究和训练，以确保其模型在明年足够好，那么这些算力将从何而来？
A: Dario, when he was on your podcast was very, very like conservative. He's like, you know, I'm not going to go crazy on compute because if my revenue inflects at a different rate at a different point, I don't want to go bankrupt. I want to make sure that we're being responsible with this scaling, but in reality, you know, he's definitely missed the pooch in terms of like going like OpenAI, which was, let's just sign these crazy deals, right. And OpenAI has kind of got way more access to compute than Anthropic by the end of the year. And so what does Anthropic have to do to get the compute? Well, they have to go to Lower quality providers that they would not have gone to before, right? Optimally, Anthropic at least historically has had the best quality providers been like Google and Amazon. Whereas, you know, at least historically minded, the biggest companies in the world, now Microsoft, and now they're expanding across the supply chain and going to other players that are newer. OpenAI has been a bit more aggressive on going to many players. Yes, they have tons of capacity from Microsoft. They have Google and Amazon as well, but they also have tons with CoreWeave and Oracle. They've gone to random companies, or one would think random companies like SoftBank Energy, who has never built a data center in their life, but they're building data centers now for OpenAI. They've gone to, and many others like Nscale and others, that they're going and getting capacity from.
A: Dario，当他出现在你的播客中时，非常非常保守。他说，你知道，我不会在算力上疯狂投入，因为如果我的收入以不同的速度在不同的时间点发生变化，我不想破产。我想确保我们在扩展方面负责任，但实际上，你知道，他肯定错过了机会，就像 OpenAI 那样，就是签订这些疯狂的协议，对吧。到今年年底，OpenAI 获得的算力比 Anthropic 多得多。那么 Anthropic 必须做些什么才能获得算力呢？他们必须去找他们以前不会去的质量较低的供应商，对吧？理想情况下，至少在历史上，Anthropic 拥有最好的质量供应商，比如谷歌和亚马逊。而至少在历史上，世界上最大的公司，现在是微软，现在他们正在扩展整个供应链，并与其他较新的参与者合作。OpenAI 在与许多参与者合作方面更加积极。是的，他们从微软获得了大量产能。他们也有谷歌和亚马逊的产能，但他们也有大量的产能来自 CoreWeave 和 Oracle。他们已经与一些随机的公司合作，或者人们会认为是一些随机的公司，比如软银能源，他们一生中从未建造过数据中心，但他们现在正在为 OpenAI 建造数据中心。他们已经与许多其他公司合作，比如 Nscale 等，他们正在从这些公司获得产能。

Q: How, specifically, has NVIDIA been able to lock up so much of both logic and memory?
Q: NVIDIA 是如何具体锁定如此多的逻辑和内存的？
A: On 3nm, if we go back to last year, the vast majority of 3nm was Apple. Apple is being moved to 2nm. Memory prices are going up, so Apple's volumes may go down because as memory prices go up, either they cut margin or they move on. There's some time lag because they have long-term contracts. But basically, Apple likely reduces demand slash moves to two nanometer faster, where two nanometer is only capable of a sort of mobile chips today. And in the future, AI chips will move there. When you look at what's TSMC running calculus here, actually, they're providing really good allocations to companies that are doing CPUs. When you think about, hey, Amazon has Tranium and Amazon has Graviton, both of those are on three nanometer, Graviton being their CPU, Tranium being their AI chip. TSMC is much more excited to give allocation to Graviton than they are to Tranium because they view CPU business as more stable, long-term growth. As a company that is conservative and doesn't want to ride cycles of growth too hard, you actually want to allocate to the market that is more stable and lower growth rate first before you allocate all the incremental capacity to the fast growth rate market. Nvidia is a bit unique because yes, they have CPUs. Yes, they make switches. Yes, they make networking. They make NVLink. They make all these different, InfiniBand, Ethernet, all these different products, NICs. By and large, most of these things will be on three nanometer by the end of this year with the Rubin launch and all the chips that are in that family, the GPU being the most important one, and yet Nvidia is getting the majority of supply. Part of this is because you look at the market and you like sort of like, you know, TSMC and others like they, there are many ways that they forecast market demand, but also it's market signal. The market signaled, hey, we need this much capacity next year. We need this much. We need this much. We'll sign non-cancelable, non-returnable. We may even pay deposits. Nvidia just did it way earlier than Google or Amazon.
A: 在 3 纳米方面，如果我们回到去年，绝大多数的 3 纳米都是苹果的。苹果正在转向 2 纳米。内存价格正在上涨，因此苹果的销量可能会下降，因为随着内存价格的上涨，要么他们削减利润，要么他们转移。这存在一些时间滞后，因为他们有长期合同。但基本上，苹果可能会减少需求，或者更快地转向 2 纳米，而 2 纳米目前只能生产移动芯片。未来，人工智能芯片将转移到那里。当你看到台积电在这里运行微积分时，实际上，他们正在为那些生产 CPU 的公司提供非常好的分配。当你想到，嘿，亚马逊有 Tranium，亚马逊有 Graviton，这两者都在 3 纳米上，Graviton 是他们的 CPU，Tranium 是他们的人工智能芯片。台积电更乐于将分配给 Graviton，而不是 Tranium，因为他们认为 CPU 业务更稳定，长期增长。作为一个保守的公司，不想过度追逐增长周期，你实际上希望首先将分配给更稳定和增长率较低的市场，然后再将所有增量产能分配给快速增长率的市场。Nvidia 有点独特，因为是的，他们有 CPU。是的，他们生产交换机。是的，他们做网络。他们生产 NVLink。他们制造所有这些不同的，InfiniBand，以太网，所有这些不同的产品，网卡。总的来说，到今年年底，随着 Rubin 的发布以及该系列中的所有芯片，这些东西中的大多数都将在 3 纳米上，其中 GPU 是最重要的，然而 Nvidia 却获得了大部分供应。部分原因是你看市场，你有点像，你知道，台积电和其他公司，他们有很多方法来预测市场需求，但这也是市场信号。市场发出了信号，嘿，我们明年需要这么多产能。我们需要这么多。我们需要这么多。我们将签署不可取消、不可退货的协议。我们甚至可能会支付定金。Nvidia 只是比谷歌或亚马逊做得更早。

Q: If EUV becomes a bottleneck, what if we just went back to 7 nanometer and do what China is doing currently in producing 7 nanometer ships with multi patterning with DUV machines; is it that bad to just bring on seven nanometer wafers and then, oh, that gives you another 50 or another 100 gigawatts?
Q: 如果 EUV 成为瓶颈，如果我们回到 7 纳米，做中国目前正在做的事情，用 DUV 机器通过多重曝光生产 7 纳米芯片，会怎么样？仅仅引入 7 纳米晶圆并增加 50 或 100 千兆瓦的算力是否很糟糕？
A: We potentially do go crazy enough that this happens because we just need incremental compute and the compute is worth the higher cost, power, etc. of these chips. But it's also unlikely to some extent, to a large extent, because of, I think, just comparing, you know, some of these are like not fair comparisons. For example, from A100, which is 312 teraflops to Blackwell, which is like 1000-ish of FP16, or maybe it's 2000 and then Rubin is like 5000 or so FP16. It's not a fair comparison because these chips have vastly different design targets. At A100, that is what Nvidia optimized for was FP16, BF16 numerics. When you look at Hopper, they didn't care as much about that. They cared about FP8. When you look at Rubin, they don't care about FP16 and BF16 as much. They care mostly about FP4 and 6. So numerics are what they've designed their chip for. Let's make a new chip design on 7 nanometers. Sure, we can do that. And then it's optimized for the numerics of the modern day. The performance difference is still going to be much larger than the flops difference you mentioned. Often, it's easy to boil things down to flops per watt or flops per dollar, but that's actually not a fair comparison. So this is where sort of you can bring in, hey, let's look at Kimi K1 or DeepSeq. When you look at Kimi or Kimi K2.5, sorry, and DeepSeq, when you look at these two models, and you look at their performance on Hopper versus Blackwell on, you know, very optimized software, you get vastly different performance. Most of this is not attributed to flops or numerics, because those models are actually 8-bit. So it's not like Blackwell's and Hopper, they're both optimized for 8-bit and Blackwell's not really taking advantage of its 4-bit there. The performance gulf is actually much larger.
A: 我们可能会变得足够疯狂以至于发生这种情况，因为我们只需要增量算力，而且这些芯片的更高成本、功率等都是值得的。但在某种程度上，在很大程度上，这也是不太可能的，因为我认为仅仅是比较，你知道，其中一些比较是不公平的。例如，从 A100（312 teraflops）到 Blackwell（大约 1000 个 FP16，或者可能是 2000 个），然后 Rubin 大约是 5000 个 FP16。这不是一个公平的比较，因为这些芯片具有截然不同的设计目标。在 A100 上，Nvidia 优化的是 FP16，BF16 数值。当你看到 Hopper 时，他们不太关心这一点。他们关心的是 FP8。当你看到 Rubin 时，他们不太关心 FP16 和 BF16。他们主要关心的是 FP4 和 6。因此，数值是他们设计芯片的目的。让我们在 7 纳米上设计一个新的芯片。当然，我们可以做到。然后它针对现代的数值进行优化。性能差异仍然会比你提到的 flops 差异大得多。通常，很容易将事情归结为每瓦 flops 或每美元 flops，但这实际上不是一个公平的比较。因此，在这里你可以引入，嘿，让我们看看 Kimi K1 或 DeepSeq。当你看到 Kimi 或 Kimi K2.5，抱歉，和 DeepSeq，当你看到这两个模型，并且你看到它们在 Hopper 与 Blackwell 上的性能，在非常优化的软件上，你会得到截然不同的性能。其中大多数不是由于 flops 或数值造成的，因为这些模型实际上是 8 位的。因此，这不像 Blackwell 和 Hopper，它们都针对 8 位进行了优化，而 Blackwell 并没有真正利用它的 4 位。性能差距实际上要大得多。

Q: If we end up in this world in 2030, where the West has the most advanced process technology, but it has not ramped it up as much, whereas China, I don't know if you think about 2030, they would have EUV and, I don't know, 2 nanometer or whatever, but they are semiconductor pilled, so they are producing in mass quantity, I'm wondering what the year is where there's a crossover where our advantage in process technology has faded enough and their advantage in scale has increased enough?
Q: 如果我们最终在 2030 年进入这个世界，西方拥有最先进的工艺技术，但还没有大量增加产量，而中国，我不知道你怎么看待 2030 年，他们将拥有 EUV，我也不知道，2 纳米或其他什么，但他们是半导体迷，所以他们正在大规模生产，我想知道在哪一年，我们在工艺技术方面的优势已经消退，而他们在规模方面的优势已经增加？
A: To date, China still does not have, you know, entire indigenized semiconductor supply chain. By 2030, it's possible that they do. To date, all of China's 7 nanometer and 14 nanometer capacity uses ASML DUV tools. And the amount that they can ship and import from ASML is large. But the point being that the vast majority of ASML's revenue, especially on EUV, all of it is outside of China. So the scale advantage is still in the favor of the, let's call it the West plus Taiwan, Japan, et cetera. They're trying to make their own DUV and EUV tools. The question is how fast can they advance and scale up production as well as quality. To date, we haven't seen that. Now, I'm quite bullish that they're gonna be able to do these things over the next five to 10 years, really scale up production, really kick it into high gear. They have more engineers working on it. They have more desire to throw capital at the problem. I think for sure, for sure, EUV, yes. And fully indigenized EUV by 2030? I think they'll have working tools. I don't think that they'll be able to manufacture a bunch yet, right? They're sort of having it work and then there's production hell, right? And ultimately, ASML had EUV working In the early 2010s, at some capacity, right? Now, the tools were not accurate enough. They were not scaled for high-volume manufacturing, reliable enough. And then they had to ramp production, and that all took time. Production hell takes time, right? Which is why it took another five to seven years to get EUV into mass production at a fab, rather than just working in the lab.
A: 迄今为止，中国仍然没有，你知道，完全本土化的半导体供应链。到 2030 年，他们有可能做到。迄今为止，中国所有的 7 纳米和 14 纳米产能都使用 ASML DUV 工具。他们可以从 ASML 运输和进口的数量很大。但关键是，ASML 的大部分收入，特别是 EUV 的收入，全部来自中国境外。因此，规模优势仍然有利于西方加上台湾、日本等。他们正在尝试制造自己的 DUV 和 EUV 工具。问题是他们能够以多快的速度推进和扩大生产以及质量。迄今为止，我们还没有看到这一点。现在，我非常乐观，他们将在未来 5 到 10 年内能够做到这些事情，真正扩大生产，真正加速发展。他们有更多的工程师在研究它。他们更渴望向这个问题投入资金。我认为肯定，肯定，EUV，是的。到 2030 年实现完全本土化的 EUV？我认为他们会拥有可用的工具。我不认为他们能够制造出一大堆，对吧？他们有点像让它工作，然后就是生产地狱，对吧？最终，ASML 在 2010 年代初就在某种程度上让 EUV 工作了，对吧？现在，这些工具不够精确。它们没有针对大批量生产进行扩展，也不够可靠。然后他们必须提高产量，而这都需要时间。生产地狱需要时间，对吧？这就是为什么又花了五到七年的时间才让 EUV 在晶圆厂大规模生产，而不仅仅是在实验室中工作。

Q: HBM is made of DRAM, but has 3 to 4x less bits per wafer area than the DRAM is made out of; is it possible that accelerators in the future could just use commodity DRAM and not HBM, and so just we can make much more capacity out of the DRAM we get?
Q: HBM 由 DRAM 制成，但每晶圆面积的比特数比 DRAM 少 3 到 4 倍；未来加速器是否可以直接使用商品 DRAM 而不是 HBM，这样我们就可以用我们获得的 DRAM 制造更多的容量？
A: I think at the end of the day, the incremental purchaser who's willing to pay the highest price for tokens also ends up being the one that's like, less price sensitive. And the compute should be allocated in a capitalistic society towards the goods that have the highest value. And the private market determines this by willingness to pay. And so to some extent, sure, Anthropic could actually release a slow mode, right? They could release Claude slow mode and have an increase in tokens per dollar by a significant amount. They could probably reduce the price of Opus 4.6 by You know, 4x, 5x, and reduce the speed by another by maybe just like 2x, like the curve on inference throughput versus speed is there already just on HBM. And yet they don't, because no one actually wants to use a slow model. And furthermore, on these agentic tasks, it's great that the model can run at this time horizon of hours. That's kind of like, okay, well, if the model was just running slower, that hours would become a day, right? Or vice versa, right? If the model is running faster, that hours becomes hour. And yet, no one really wants to move to that day-long wait period because the highest value tasks also have some time sensitivity to them. And so I struggle to see, you know, yes, you could use DDR. But then there's a couple like things that are challenging with this, right? You could use regular DRAM.
A: 我认为归根结底，愿意为 tokens 支付最高价格的增量购买者最终也是对价格不太敏感的人。算力应该在一个资本主义社会中分配给具有最高价值的商品。私人市场通过支付意愿来决定这一点。因此，在某种程度上，当然，Anthropic 实际上可以发布一个慢速模式，对吧？他们可以发布 Claude 慢速模式，并显著增加每美元的 tokens 数量。他们可能会将 Opus 4.6 的价格降低 4 倍、5 倍，并将速度降低 2 倍，仅仅在 HBM 上，推理吞吐量与速度之间的曲线就已经存在了。然而他们没有这样做，因为实际上没有人想使用慢速模型。此外，在这些代理任务中，模型可以在几个小时的时间范围内运行是很棒的。这有点像，好吧，如果模型运行得更慢，那么几个小时将变成一天，对吧？反之亦然，对吧？如果模型运行得更快，那么几个小时将变成一个小时。然而，没有人真正想转移到那一天的等待时间，因为最有价值的任务也对时间有一定的敏感性。因此，我很难看到，你知道，是的，你可以使用 DDR。但是有一些事情是具有挑战性的，对吧？你可以使用常规 DRAM。

Q: What does this imply for the next year or two as this memory crunch hits?
Q: 这对未来一两年意味着什么，因为内存危机正在冲击？
A: Memory crunch will continue to be harder and harder, and prices continue to go up. And this affects different parts of the market differently. Gets to sort of the like, are people going to hate AI more and more? Yes, because now smartphones and PCs are not going to get incrementally better year on year. And in fact, they're getting incrementally worse. If you look at the bill of materials of an iPhone, what fraction of it is the memory? Like how much more expensive does an iPhone get if the memory is 2x more expensive or whatever it has to be? I believe an iPhone has 12 gigabytes of memory. Each gig used to cost roughly  4, so it's  150 versus  100 increase in cost on Apple. Also, Apple has some margin, they're not just going to eat the margin. So now that's  150 increase on the iPhone. Apple has to either pass it on to the consumer, A, Or B, they have to eat it. I don't see Apple reducing their margin too much. Maybe they eat a little bit. But at the end of the day, that means the end consumer is paying $250 more for an iPhone. And now that's on like, hey, what is last year's memory pricing versus today's? Now, there is some lag for Apple to have to feel the heat because they have tended to have, you know, three, six or a year long contracts for a lot of memory. But at the end of the day, Apple gets hit pretty hard by this.
A: 内存危机将继续变得越来越严重，价格将继续上涨。这会以不同的方式影响市场的不同部分。这有点像，人们会越来越讨厌人工智能吗？是的，因为现在智能手机和 PC 不会逐年变得更好。事实上，它们正在变得越来越糟。如果你看一下 iPhone 的物料清单，其中有多少是内存？如果内存贵两倍或必须贵多少，iPhone 会贵多少？我相信 iPhone 有 12GB 的内存。每个 GB 过去大约花费 3 或 4 美元，所以是 50 美元。但现在内存的价格大约是三倍，如果现在是 DDR，我们称之为每个 GB 12 美元。所以现在你说的是 150 美元对 50 美元，对吧？苹果的成本增加了 100 美元。此外，苹果也有一些利润，他们不会仅仅吞下利润。所以现在成本增加了 100 美元。这仅仅是在 DRAM 上。NAND 也有类似的市场。所以实际上，你知道，iPhone 的成本可能会增加 150 美元。苹果要么将其转嫁给消费者，要么必须吞下它。我不认为苹果会大幅降低他们的利润。也许他们会吞下一点。但归根结底，这意味着最终消费者要为 iPhone 多支付 250 美元。现在这是关于去年内存定价与今天的比较。现在，苹果需要一段时间才能感受到热度，因为他们倾向于为大量内存签订三、六个月或一年的合同。但归根结底，苹果会受到相当大的打击。

Q: If you're saying, look, the memory logic, et cetera, the N3 is mostly going to be AI accelerators, but then there's N2, which is mostly Apple now, and then in the future, I guess AI would also want to go on N2, can they kick out Apple if Nvidia and Amazon and Google say, hey, we're willing to pay a lot of money for N2 capacity?
Q: 如果你说，你看，内存逻辑等，N3 主要用于人工智能加速器，但 N2 主要用于苹果，然后在未来，我想人工智能也想使用 N2，如果 Nvidia、亚马逊和谷歌说，嘿，我们愿意为 N2 产能支付很多钱，他们能把苹果踢出去吗？
A: I think the challenge of this is chip design timelines take a long while. And so that's more than a year. And the designs that are on two nanometer are more than a year out. And so what would really happen is Apple or sorry, Nvidia and all these others will be like, hey, we're going to prepay for the capacity and you're going to expand it for us. And then Apple will be, and maybe TSMC takes a little bit of margin, but not a ton. They're not going to kick Apple out entirely, right? What they're going to do is when Apple orders X, they may say, hey, we project you only need Y or X minus one. And so that's what we're going to give you is X minus one. And then that flex capacity Apple's kind of screwed on. Whereas traditionally Apple's always overordered by like 10% and cut back by 10% over the course of the year. And some years they hit the entire 10%, just, you know, volumes vary, right? Based on the season and macro, blah, blah, blah, blah, blah. And so I don't think TSMC would kick out Apple. I think Apple will become a smaller and smaller and smaller percentage of TSMC's revenue and therefore be less relevant for TSMC to cater to their demands. And TSMC could eventually start saying, hey, you've got to pre-book your capacity for next year, for two years out, and you have to pre-pay for the CapEx because that's what Nvidia and Amazon and Google are doing.
A: 我认为这里的挑战是芯片设计的时间线很长。这超过一年。在两纳米上的设计已经超过一年了。因此，真正发生的是苹果或者抱歉，Nvidia 和其他所有这些公司会说，嘿，我们将预付产能的费用，你们将为我们扩大产能。然后苹果会说，也许台积电会拿走一点利润，但不会太多。他们不会完全把苹果踢出去，对吧？他们要做的是，当苹果订购 X 时，他们可能会说，嘿，我们预计你只需要 Y 或 X 减 1。所以我们将给你的就是 X 减 1。然后苹果的那部分灵活产能就被搞砸了。而传统上，苹果总是超额订购 10%，并在一年内削减 10%。有些年份他们达到了整个 10%，只是，你知道，销量会发生变化，对吧？基于季节和宏观经济等等。因此，我不认为台积电会把苹果踢出去。我认为苹果在台积电收入中所占的比例会越来越小，因此台积电满足他们的需求变得越来越不重要。台积电最终可能会开始说，嘿，你必须预订明年的产能，提前两年预订，而且你必须预先支付资本支出，因为 Nvidia、亚马逊和谷歌就是这样做的。

Q: What is preventing ASML from producing more than 100 EUV machines in 2030, and why are you so confident that even five years out, you can be relatively sure what their production will be?
Q: 是什么阻止了 ASML 在 2030 年生产超过 100 台 EUV 机器，为什么你如此自信，即使在五年后，你也能相对确定他们的产量？
A: ASML has not decided to just go YOLO, let's expand capacity as fast as possible. In general, the semiconductor supply chain has not. It's lived through the booms and busts. And we can talk a bit more about it. But basically, no one, you know, some players as of very recently have like woken up, but in general, no one really sees demand for 200 gigawatts a year of AI chips or, you know, trillions of dollars of spend a year in the semiconductor supply chain. They're just like, they're not, they're not AI-filled, right? They're not AGI-filled. ASML, Their tool has four major components. It has the source, which is made by CYMER in San Diego. It has the reticle stage, which is made in Wilmington, Connecticut. It has the wafer stage. And the optics, right, the lenses and such, and those two are made in Europe, right? And so when you look at each of these four, they're tremendously complex supply chains that A, they have not tried to expand massively, and B, when they try to expand them, the time lag is quite long. And so again, this is the most complicated machine that humans make, period, right, at a volume, At any sort of volume, but like, let's talk about the source specifically, right?
A: ASML 还没有决定放手一搏，让我们尽可能快地扩大产能。一般来说，半导体供应链还没有。它经历了繁荣和萧条。我们可以多谈谈这个问题。但基本上，没有人，你知道，最近的一些参与者已经醒悟了，但总的来说，没有人真正看到每年对人工智能芯片的需求达到 200 千兆瓦，或者每年在半导体供应链中花费数万亿美元。他们只是，他们没有被人工智能填满，对吧？他们没有被 AGI 填满。ASML 的工具包含四个主要组成部分。它有光源，由圣地亚哥的 CYMER 制造。它有掩模台，在康涅狄格州威尔明顿制造。它有晶圆台。还有光学器件，透镜等等，后两者是在欧洲制造的，对吧？因此，当你看到这四个组成部分中的每一个时，它们都是非常复杂的供应链，A，他们没有尝试大规模扩张，B，当他们尝试扩张时，时间滞后相当长。因此，再次，这是人类制造的最复杂的机器，句号，对吧，以一定的量，以任何一种量，但就像，让我们具体谈谈光源，对吧？

Q: If we believe that tools are the ultimate bottleneck, How much of Taiwan's place in the semiconductor supply chain could we de-risk simply by having a plan to airlift every single process engineer or TSMC out when things come to, if they get blockaded or something, or do you actually still need to ship out the EUV tools, which would be multiple plane loads per single tool and would not be practical?
Q: 如果我们相信工具是最终的瓶颈，仅仅通过制定计划，在事情发生时，将每一位工艺工程师或台积电的人员空运出去，或者他们被封锁或其他什么，我们可以在多大程度上降低台湾在半导体供应链中的地位风险？或者你实际上仍然需要运出 EUV 工具，这需要多架飞机的装载量才能运出一台工具，这并不实际？
A: If you ship out all the process engineers and assuming it's like hot enough that you destroy the fabs, no one has all the fabs in Taiwan now. Which is a big risk, right? These tools actually use a lot of semiconductors which are manufactured in Taiwan. It's like a snake eating its own tail sort of like meme because you can't make the tools without the chips from Taiwan which you can't use without the tools in Taiwan. There's obviously some diversification there but And they don't use super advanced chips in lithography tools, but at the end of the day, there is some tail eating the dragon. Just shipping out all the engineers and blowing up the fabs means China has a stronger semiconductor supply chain than the rest of the world, right? In terms of verticalization, now that you've removed Taiwan, and now you've got all the know-how, but you've got to replicate it in, let's say, Arizona or wherever for TSMC. And it's going to take a long time to build all the capacity that TSMC has had built over the years. And so you've drastically slowed US and global GDP, not just growth, you've shrank the GDP massively. And you've got a lot bigger problems. And your incremental ability to add compute goes to almost zero, right? Instead of hundreds of gigawatts a year by the end of decade, let's say by the end of the decade, something happens to Taiwan. Now you're at maybe like 10 gigawatts across Intel and Samsung or 20 gigawatts. It's like nothing. But now all of a sudden you've like really caused some crazy dynamics in AI.
A: 如果你运出所有的工艺工程师，并假设情况足够严重，以至于你摧毁了晶圆厂，现在没有人在台湾拥有所有的晶圆厂。这是一个很大的风险，对吧？这些工具实际上使用了许多在台湾制造的半导体。这就像一条蛇吃自己的尾巴，因为没有来自台湾的芯片，你就无法制造这些工具，而没有台湾的工具，你就无法使用这些芯片。显然存在一些多元化，而且它们在光刻工具中不使用超级先进的芯片，但归根结底，存在一些尾巴吃龙的情况。仅仅运出所有的工程师并炸毁晶圆厂意味着中国的半导体供应链比世界其他地区更强大，对吧？就垂直化而言，既然你已经移除了台湾，现在你已经掌握了所有的技术，但你必须在亚利桑那州或其他地方复制它给台积电。而且建立台积电多年来建立的所有产能需要很长时间。因此，你大大减缓了美国和全球的 GDP，不仅仅是增长，你还大幅缩小了 GDP。而且你遇到了更大的问题。你增加计算能力的能力几乎降至零，对吧？而不是到本十年末每年增加数百千兆瓦，假设到本十年末，台湾发生了什么事情。现在你可能只有 10 千兆瓦，英特尔和三星有 20 千兆瓦。这就像什么都没有。但现在突然间，你在人工智能领域造成了一些疯狂的动态。

Q: Is it possible that accelerators in the future could just use commodity DRAM and not HBM, and so just we can make much more capacity out of the DRAM we get, and what is the bandwidth difference between HBM and a normal DRAM?
Q: 未来加速器是否有可能只使用普通 DRAM 而不使用 HBM，这样我们就可以从 DRAM 中获得更大的容量？HBM 和普通 DRAM 之间的带宽差异是多少？
A: You could use regular DRAM. One is you're still limited, you know, one of the like core constraints of chips, even though they're, you know, sort of like, you know, a chip is like a certain size, all of the IO escapes on the edges of the chip, right? So oftentimes, you know, what you see is the left and the right of the chip are HBM, the IO from the chip to the HBM is on the sides and then the top and bottom are IO to other chips, right? And so if you were to change from HBM to DDR, then all of a sudden this IO on this edge would have significantly less bandwidth, but it had significantly more capacity per chip. And so yes, you're making less You know, the metric that you actually care about is bandwidth per wafer, not bits per wafer. If you switch to DDR, yes, you produce 4x the bits, per DRAM wafer, but all of a sudden the constraints shift a lot and your system design shifts a lot. You go slower. Yes. Is the market smaller? Okay, maybe possibly, but also now all of a sudden all these flops are wasted because they're just sitting there waiting for memory. It's like great. I don't need all that capacity because I can't really increase batch size because then the KV cache is going to take even longer to read. An HBM stack of HBM4 is 2048 bits across connected in an area that's like 13 millimeters wide. So 2048 bits and it transfers memory at around 10 gigatransfers a second. So, a stack of HBM4 is 2048 bits on an area that's 13 millimeters wide, roughly, or 11. And that's the shoreline that you're taking on the chip. And in that shoreline, you have 2048 bits transferring at 10 gigatransfers per second. You multiply those together and you divide by 8 bits to bytes. You're at roughly 2.5 terabytes a second per HBM stack. When you look at DDR, in that same area, it's maybe 64 or 128 bits wide. And that DDR5 is transferring at anywhere from 6.4 gigatransfers a second to maybe 8,000 gigatransfers a second. So your bandwidth is significantly lower. It's 64 times 8,000 divided by 8. You're at 64 gigabytes a second. And even if you take a generous interpretation of 128 times 8 gigatransfers, you're at 128 gigabytes a second for the same shoreline versus two and a half terabytes a second. There's an order of magnitude difference in bandwidth per edge area.
A: 你可以使用普通 DRAM。但你仍然会受到限制，你知道，芯片的核心约束之一是，即使它们，你知道，有点像，你知道，一个芯片有一定的尺寸，所有的 IO 都从芯片的边缘逃逸，对吧？所以通常，你知道，你看到的是芯片的左边和右边是 HBM，芯片到 HBM 的 IO 在两侧，然后顶部和底部是到其他芯片的 IO，对吧？所以，如果你从 HBM 改为 DDR，那么这条边上的 IO 的带宽会大大降低，但每个芯片的容量会大大增加。所以，是的，你做的少了。你知道，你真正关心的指标是每晶圆的带宽，而不是每晶圆的比特数。如果你切换到 DDR，是的，你生产的比特数是 DRAM 晶圆的 4 倍，但突然间，约束条件发生了很大的变化，你的系统设计也发生了很大的变化。你变慢了。是的。市场变小了吗？好吧，也许有可能，但现在突然间，所有的 flops 都被浪费了，因为它们只是坐在那里等待内存。这太棒了。我不需要所有的容量，因为我无法真正增加批量大小，因为那样 KV 缓存需要更长的时间来读取。一个 HBM4 的 HBM 堆栈是 2048 位，连接在一个大约 13 毫米宽的区域内。因此，2048 位，它以大约每秒 10 千兆传输的速度传输内存。所以，一个 HBM4 的堆栈是 2048 位，在一个大约 13 毫米宽的区域内，大约是 11 毫米。这是你在芯片上占据的海岸线。在那条海岸线上，你有 2048 位以每秒 10 千兆传输的速度传输。你把它们乘起来，然后除以 8 位来得到字节。你大约是每 HBM 堆栈每秒 2.5TB。当你观察 DDR 时，在同一区域内，它可能是 64 或 128 位宽。DDR5 的传输速度在每秒 6.4 千兆传输到可能 8000 千兆传输之间。所以你的带宽明显较低。它是 64 乘以 8000 除以 8。你每秒的速度是 64GB。即使你对 128 乘以 8 千兆传输进行慷慨的解释，你每秒的速度也是 128GB，而相同的海岸线是每秒 2.5TB。每边缘区域的带宽存在一个数量级的差异。

Q: What is preventing us from just doing that with How many dies could you have a single chip and still get these tens of terabytes a second?
Q: 是什么阻止我们用多少个 die 制造一个芯片，仍然能达到每秒数十 TB 的速度？
A: Even within Blackwell, there are differences in performance when you're communicating on the chip versus across the chips. Those bounds are obviously much smaller than when you're going out of the entire chip, but each die versus within the package. And so anyways, when you scale the number of chips up, there is some performance loss. It's not just perfect, but it is way better than different entire packages. Now, how large can advanced packaging scale? The way Nvidia is doing it is CoOS, the way Google and with Broadcom and MediaTek and Amazon, Tranium, all these chips are doing is called CoOS. But actually you can go and look back at what Tesla did with Dojo, right? Dojo, which they canceled and restarted. Anyways, Dojo was a chip that was the size of an entire wafer. They had 25 chips on it. And there were some trade-offs, right? They couldn't put HBM on it. But the positive side of it was that they had 25 chips on it. And so to date, it is still probably the best chip for running convolutional neural networks. It's just not great at transformers because the, you know, the sort of the shape of the chip, the memory, the arithmetic, all these various specifications of it are just not well suited for transformers. They're well suited for CNNs.
A: 即使在 Blackwell 内部，在芯片上通信和跨芯片通信时，性能也存在差异。这些界限显然比你离开整个芯片时要小得多，但每个 die 与封装内部相比也是如此。所以无论如何，当你扩大芯片数量时，性能会损失一些。它不是完美的，但它比不同的整个封装要好得多。现在，先进封装可以扩展到多大？英伟达的做法是 CoOS，谷歌以及博通、联发科和亚马逊，Tranium，所有这些芯片都在做的是叫做 CoOS。但实际上你可以回顾一下特斯拉用 Dojo 做了什么，对吧？Dojo，他们取消并重新启动了。无论如何，Dojo 是一个芯片，它的大小相当于整个晶圆。他们上面有 25 个芯片。并且存在一些权衡，对吧？他们不能在上面放置 HBM。但积极的一面是他们上面有 25 个芯片。所以到目前为止，它仍然可能是运行卷积神经网络的最佳芯片。它只是不擅长 transformers，因为芯片的形状、内存、算术，所有这些不同的规格都不太适合 transformers。它们非常适合 CNN。

Q: If by 2030 there's millions of humanoids running around, which each need local compute, any thoughts on what that implies, and what will be required for that?
Q: 如果到 2030 年有数百万个人形机器人四处走动，每个都需要本地计算，你对这意味着什么以及需要什么有什么想法？
A: To some extent, you don't need to have all the intelligence in the robot. And it would be much more efficient to not do that, right? Because in the server, in cloud, you can batch process and all these things. So what you may want to do is, hey, a lot of the planning and longer horizon tasks are determined by a much more capable model in the cloud that runs at very high batch sizes. And then it pushes those directions to the robots who then interpolate between each subsequent action or is given like, hey, pick up that cup and then the model on the robot can pick up the cup. And it's like, as it's picking up, it's like, oh, you know, in fact, this, you know, you know, things like weight and all these things might have to be and like force may have to be like, determined by the model on the robot, but not everything needs to be like, you know, hey, pick up the robot, you know, this, right? Or like, hey, that's a headphone. Actually, I'm the supermodel in the cloud. I know that this headphones are, you know, Sony, XM6 is, which is not a Dwarkesh ad spot, but you know. It might say, hey, the headband is soft and this is the weight of it and all these things. And then the model on the robot can be less intelligent and take these inputs and do the actions. And it may get told by the model in the cloud every second, every 10 times a second, maybe, you know, depends on the hertz of the action, but a lot of that can be offloaded to the cloud.
A: 在某种程度上，你不需要在机器人中拥有所有的智能。不这样做会更有效率，对吧？因为在服务器、在云中，你可以批量处理所有这些事情。所以你可能想要做的是，嘿，许多规划和更长远的 horizon 任务是由云中一个更强大的模型决定的，该模型以非常高的批量大小运行。然后它将这些方向推送到机器人，然后机器人在每个后续动作之间进行插值，或者被告知，嘿，拿起那个杯子，然后机器人上的模型可以拿起杯子。当它拿起时，它就像，哦，你知道，事实上，这，你知道，诸如重量之类的事情以及所有这些事情可能必须是，并且像力一样，可能必须由机器人上的模型来确定，但不是所有的事情都需要像，你知道，嘿，拿起机器人，你知道，这，对吧？或者像，嘿，那是耳机。实际上，我是云中的超级模型。我知道这款耳机是索尼的 XM6，这不是 Dwarkesh 广告位，但你知道。它可能会说，嘿，头带是柔软的，这是它的重量以及所有这些事情。然后机器人上的模型可以不那么智能，并接受这些输入并执行动作。它可能会被云中的模型每秒、每秒 10 次告知，也许，你知道，取决于动作的赫兹，但很多都可以卸载到云端。

Q: What are the reasons you’re skeptical of space data centers?
Q: 你对太空数据中心持怀疑态度的原因是什么？
A: Even if power costs double, you're still at a fraction of the total cost of the GPU. The main challenge is And what we've seen that disperses, right? We have ClusterMax, which rates all the Neo clouds and we test them. We test over 40 cloud companies, including the hyperscalers and Neo clouds. What differentiates some of these clouds the most outside of software is their ability to deploy and manage failure, right? GPUs are horrendously unreliable. Even today, 15% of black wells or so that get deployed have to be RMA'd. You have to take them out. You have to, you know, maybe just plug them and plug them back in, but sometimes you have to take them out and ship them to Nvidia or rather their partners who do these RMAs and such. And if your argument is that, you know, hey, GPUs have a useful life of X years, right? If a GPU has a useful life of five years, and it takes three additional months, probably six, let's say six additional months, then that is 10% of your cluster's useful life. And because we're so capacity constrained, that compute is most valuable Theoretically, in the first six months you have it because we're more constrained now than in the future because that compute now can contribute to a better model in the future or contribute to revenue now, which you can use to raise more money to get better, you know, all these sorts of things. Now is always the most important moment. And so you've delayed your compute deployment by six months potentially. And the thing that separates these clouds is we see clouds that take six months to deploy GPUs today on earth, right? We see clouds that take a lot less than six months, right? And so the question is, where does space get in there? I don't see how you would test them all on Earth, deconstruct them and ship them into space. And it not take longer than just putting them in the spot that you're testing them.
A: 即使电力成本翻倍，你仍然只占 GPU 总成本的一小部分。主要的挑战是，我们已经看到分散了，对吧？我们有 ClusterMax，它对所有 Neo 云进行评级，我们测试它们。我们测试了 40 多家云公司，包括超大规模企业和 Neo 云。除了软件之外，区分这些云的最大因素是它们部署和管理故障的能力，对吧？GPU 非常不可靠。即使在今天，部署的 black wells 中大约有 15% 必须进行 RMA。你必须把它们拿出来。你必须，你知道，也许只是插上它们然后再插回去，但有时你必须把它们拿出来并运送到英伟达或他们的合作伙伴那里进行这些 RMA 等。如果你的论点是，你知道，嘿，GPU 的有用寿命是 X 年，对吧？如果一个 GPU 的有用寿命是五年，并且需要额外三个月，可能六个月，假设是六个月，那么这占你集群有用寿命的 10%。而且因为我们的容量非常有限，所以计算在理论上在你拥有的前六个月最有价值，因为我们现在比将来更受限制，因为现在的计算可以为将来更好的模型做出贡献，或者为现在的收入做出贡献，你可以用这些收入来筹集更多的资金来获得更好的，你知道，所有这些事情。现在永远是最重要的时刻。因此，你可能会将计算部署推迟六个月。区分这些云的一点是，我们看到一些云在地球上需要六个月的时间来部署 GPU，对吧？我们看到一些云需要的时间远少于六个月，对吧？所以问题是，太空在哪里介入？我不明白你如何在地球上测试它们，拆解它们并将它们运送到太空。而且它不会比仅仅将它们放在你正在测试它们的地方花费更长的时间。

Q: So you say we're producing 60 of these machines this year and then 70, 80 over subsequent years, what would happen if ASML just decided to double its CapEx or triple its CapEx?
Q: 所以你说我们今年生产 60 台这样的机器，然后在随后的几年里生产 70、80 台，如果 ASML 决定将其资本支出增加一倍或三倍会发生什么？
A: ASML has not decided to just go YOLO, let's expand capacity as fast as possible. In general, the semiconductor supply chain has not, right? It's lived through the booms and busts. And we can talk a bit more about it. But basically, no one, you know, some players as of very recently have like woken up, but in general, no one really sees demand for 200 gigawatts a year of AI chips or, you know, trillions of dollars of spend a year in the semiconductor supply chain. They're just like, they're not, they're not AI-filled, right? They're not AGI-filled. ASML, Their tool has four major components. It has the source, which is made by CYMER in San Diego. It has the reticle stage, which is made in Wilmington, Connecticut. It has the wafer stage. And the optics, right, the lenses and such, and those two are made in Europe, right? And so when you look at each of these four, they're tremendously complex supply chains that A, they have not tried to expand massively, and B, when they try to expand them, the time lag is quite long. And so again, this is the most complicated machine that humans make, period, right, at a volume, At any sort of volume, but like, let's talk about the source specifically, right?
A: ASML 并没有决定直接 YOLO，让我们尽可能快地扩大产能。总的来说，半导体供应链没有这样做，对吧？它经历了繁荣和萧条。我们可以更多地谈论它。但基本上，没有人，你知道，一些参与者直到最近才醒悟过来，但总的来说，没有人真正看到每年对 200 千兆瓦人工智能芯片的需求，或者每年在半导体供应链中花费数万亿美元的需求。他们只是，他们不是人工智能驱动的，对吧？他们不是 AGI 驱动的。ASML，他们的工具有四个主要组成部分。它有光源，由圣地亚哥的 CYMER 制造。它有掩模台，在康涅狄格州威明顿制造。它有晶圆台。以及光学器件，对吧，透镜等，这两者都在欧洲制造，对吧？因此，当你观察这四个中的每一个时，它们都是极其复杂的供应链，A，它们没有尝试大规模扩张，并且 B，当它们尝试扩张时，时间滞后相当长。所以再次强调，这是人类制造的最复杂的机器，句号，对吧，在一个量上，在任何量上，但比如，让我们具体谈谈光源，对吧？

Q: If it takes 4X more wafer area to get the same byte for HBM, you had to destroy 4X as much consumer demand for laptops and phones and whatever in order to free up one byte for AI, what does this imply for the next year or two?
Q: 如果获得相同字节的 HBM 需要 4 倍的晶圆面积，你必须摧毁 4 倍的消费者对笔记本电脑和手机等的需求，才能为 AI 腾出一个字节，这对未来一两年意味着什么？

And in fact, they're getting incrementally worse. If you look at

Keywords


Keywords

Explanation

SemiAnalysis

Dylan Patel's company that provides in-depth research and analysis of the semiconductor industry. SemiAnalysis produces reports and data used by companies and investors to understand trends in the semiconductor market.

SemiAnalysis

Dylan Patel 的公司，提供对半导体行业的深入研究和分析。SemiAnalysis 产出报告和数据，供公司和投资者了解半导体市场的趋势。

Capex

Capital expenditures, which are funds used by a company to acquire, upgrade, and maintain physical assets such as property, buildings, or equipment. The combined forecasted capex of Amazon, Meta, Google, and Microsoft is $600 billion this year.

Capex

资本支出，即公司用于购买、升级和维护有形资产（如财产、建筑物或设备）的资金。预计今年亚马逊、Meta、谷歌和微软的资本支出总额为 6000 亿美元。

Hyperscalers

Large companies that provide cloud computing and internet-based services. These companies, including Amazon, Google, and Microsoft, operate massive data centers and drive significant demand in the semiconductor industry.

Hyperscalers

提供云计算和互联网服务的大型公司。这些公司，包括亚马逊、谷歌和微软，运营着庞大的数据中心，并推动了半导体行业的巨大需求。

Power Purchasing Agreements (PPAs)

Long-term contracts used by companies to buy electricity directly from energy generators. These agreements help companies secure stable energy supplies and can support the development of renewable energy projects.

Power Purchasing Agreements (PPAs)

公司用来直接从能源生产商那里购买电力的长期合同。这些协议帮助公司获得稳定的能源供应，并可以支持可再生能源项目的发展。

NeoCloud

A term used to describe smaller, newer cloud computing providers that often specialize in specific services, such as AI compute. These companies often offer more flexible or specialized compute options compared to larger hyperscalers.

NeoCloud

一个用来描述规模较小、较新的云计算提供商的术语，它们通常专注于特定服务，例如 AI 计算。与大型超大规模企业相比，这些公司通常提供更灵活或更专业的计算选项。

Hopper/Blackwell/Rubin

Generations of high-performance GPUs designed by Nvidia for AI and machine learning workloads. Each generation features advancements in processing power, memory bandwidth, and architectural improvements.

Hopper/Blackwell/Rubin

英伟达为人工智能和机器学习工作负载设计的高性能 GPU 的几代产品。每一代产品都在处理能力、内存带宽和架构改进方面有所进步。

EUV (Extreme Ultraviolet) Lithography

An advanced technology used in semiconductor manufacturing to create extremely fine patterns on silicon wafers. ASML is the primary manufacturer of EUV lithography machines, which are essential for producing leading-edge chips.

EUV (Extreme Ultraviolet) Lithography

半导体制造中使用的一种先进技术，用于在硅晶圆上创建非常精细的图案。ASML 是 EUV 光刻机的主要制造商，这些光刻机对于生产领先芯片至关重要。

ASML

A Dutch company that is the world's leading manufacturer of lithography systems, especially those using extreme ultraviolet (EUV) light. These systems are essential for producing advanced semiconductors.

ASML

一家荷兰公司，是世界领先的光刻系统制造商，尤其是使用极紫外 (EUV) 光的系统。这些系统对于生产先进半导体至关重要。

TSMC (Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Company)

The world's largest dedicated independent semiconductor foundry. TSMC manufactures chips for a wide range of customers, including Apple, Nvidia, and AMD.

TSMC (Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Company)

世界最大的专业独立半导体代工厂。台积电为包括苹果、英伟达和 AMD 在内的众多客户制造芯片。

HBM (High Bandwidth Memory)

A type of high-performance memory used in GPUs and other processors to provide fast data access. HBM is essential for AI and machine learning workloads that require high memory bandwidth.

HBM (High Bandwidth Memory)

一种用于 GPU 和其他处理器中的高性能内存，以提供快速的数据访问。HBM 对于需要高内存带宽的 AI 和机器学习工作负载至关重要。

ARR (Annual Recurring Revenue)

A metric used to measure the value of subscription-based businesses. For example, Google's Gemini ARRs.

ARR（年度经常性收入）

一种用于衡量基于订阅的业务价值的指标。例如，谷歌的 Gemini ARR。

AGI (Artificial General Intelligence)

A hypothetical level of AI that possesses human-like general intelligence and can perform any intellectual task that a human being can.

AGI（通用人工智能）

一种假想的人工智能水平，它拥有类似人类的通用智能，并且可以执行人类可以执行的任何智力任务。

Hyperscaler and AI Lab Compute Spending: Timelines and Investment Strategies
超级计算和人工智能实验室的计算支出：时间表和投资策略
Dwarkesh and Dylan discuss the forecasted capital expenditures (CapEx) of major tech companies like Amazon, Meta, Google, and Microsoft, totaling  110 billion) and Anthropic ($30 billion) and question how these funds align with their current compute spending. Dwarkesh seeks to understand the timeline for when the big tech CapEx will translate into actual compute availability and what the AI labs are planning to use their raised capital for, considering the cost of data centers.
Dwarkesh 和 Dylan 讨论了主要科技公司（如亚马逊、Meta、谷歌和微软）预计的资本支出（CapEx），今年总计 6000 亿美元，以及这与即将上线的计算能力有何关系。他们还研究了 OpenAI（1100 亿美元）和 Anthropic（300 亿美元）等人工智能实验室筹集的大量资金，并质疑这些资金如何与他们目前的计算支出相符。Dwarkesh 试图了解大型科技公司的资本支出何时转化为实际的计算可用性，以及考虑到数据中心的成本，人工智能实验室计划如何使用他们筹集的资金。

Hyperscaler CapEx Allocation and Anthropic's Compute Needs for Revenue Growth
超级计算公司的资本支出分配和 Anthropic 实现收入增长所需的计算能力
Dylan explains that the $600 billion CapEx figure is part of a larger trillion-dollar investment across the supply chain, with some portion immediately allocated to compute going online this year. However, a significant portion is for future setup, including turbine deposits and data center construction for subsequent years. He notes that Anthropic and OpenAI are major customers, currently using around 2 gigawatts each, but aiming to scale much larger. Dylan estimates that Anthropic needs to add 4 gigawatts of inference capacity to support projected revenue growth, potentially requiring them to exceed 5 gigawatts by year-end.
Dylan 解释说，6000 亿美元的资本支出是整个供应链中更大的万亿美元投资的一部分，其中一部分立即分配给今年上线的计算。然而，很大一部分用于未来的设置，包括涡轮机押金和后续几年的数据中心建设。他指出，Anthropic 和 OpenAI 是主要客户，目前各自使用约 2 吉瓦，但目标是扩大规模。Dylan 估计，Anthropic 需要增加 4 吉瓦的推理能力来支持预计的收入增长，可能需要他们在年底前超过 5 吉瓦。

Anthropic's Compute Constraints and OpenAI's Aggressive Acquisition Strategy
Anthropic 的计算约束和 OpenAI 的积极收购策略
Dylan discusses Anthropic's conservative approach to compute acquisition, contrasting it with OpenAI's aggressive strategy of securing numerous deals. Due to this conservatism, Anthropic may need to turn to lower-quality compute providers. OpenAI, on the other hand, has diversified its compute sources, including Microsoft, Google, Amazon, CoreWeave, Oracle, and even SoftBank Energy. Dylan explains that Anthropic's caution stemmed from financial concerns in the previous year, where some companies feared end buyers wouldn't be able to pay for signed compute deals.
Dylan 讨论了 Anthropic 在计算收购方面采取的保守方法，并将其与 OpenAI 积极达成多项交易的策略进行了对比。由于这种保守主义，Anthropic 可能需要转向质量较低的计算提供商。另一方面，OpenAI 使其计算来源多样化，包括微软、谷歌、亚马逊、CoreWeave、甲骨文，甚至软银能源。Dylan 解释说，Anthropic 的谨慎源于去年的财务担忧，当时一些公司担心最终买家无法支付已签署的计算协议。

OpenAI's Early Compute Lock-In and the Depreciation Cycle of GPUs

Dylan notes that OpenAI faced initial skepticism from compute providers but is now seen as a reliable partner due to its funding. Dwarkesh raises the question of GPU depreciation cycles, noting that while some bears argue for shorter cycles, Dylan suggests that the depreciation cycle might be even longer than five years, especially if older GPUs like Hoppers and A100s remain valuable in the future.
Dylan 指出，OpenAI 最初受到计算提供商的怀疑，但由于其资金充足，现在被视为可靠的合作伙伴。他还指出，Anthropic 的收入增长速度超过了计算能力的可用性。Dwarkesh 提出了 GPU 折旧周期的问题，指出虽然一些空头认为周期较短，但 Dylan 认为折旧周期可能比五年还要长，特别是如果像 Hoppers 和 A100 这样的旧 GPU 在未来仍然有价值。

(10:46)
which increases the sort of like reported amortized CapEx in a given year. And so it makes it maybe financially less lucrative to building all these clouds. GPU Depreciation, Total Cost of Ownership, and the Value of Utility
GPU 折旧、总拥有成本以及效用的价值
Dylan estimates Anthropic will reach 5 gigawatts by year-end through their own capacity and partnerships. He then addresses Michael Burry's argument for a three-year GPU depreciation cycle, explaining the TCO model and how it builds up the hourly cost of a GPU. He contrasts this with the utility derived from the chip, arguing that the value of an H100 is now predicated on the value that GPT-5.4 can get out of it instead of the value that GPT-4 can get out of it.
Dylan 估计，到年底，Anthropic 将通过其自身的能力和合作伙伴关系达到 5 吉瓦。然后，他谈到了 Michael Burry 关于三年 GPU 折旧周期的论点，解释了 TCO 模型以及它如何构建 GPU 的每小时成本。他将其与芯片的效用进行了对比，认为 H100 的价值现在取决于 GPT-5.4 可以从中获得的价值，而不是 GPT-4 可以从中获得的价值。
Dylan Patel:
(11:21)
There's a few strings to pull on there. One is what happens to depreciation of GPUs, right? And I guess I didn't answer your prior question, which is like anthropic I think we'll be able to get to like five gigawatts-ish, maybe a little bit more by the end of the year, through themselves as well as their product being served through Bedrock or through Vertex or through Foundry. I think they'll be able to get to five or six gigawatts, which is way above their initial plans, right? And anyways, that's sort of like, and OpenAI will be roughly the same, maybe a little higher, actually a little bit higher based on our numbers. Anyways, the depreciation cycle of a GPU, right?
这里有一些可以利用的点。其中一点是 GPU 的折旧会发生什么，对吧？我想我没有回答你之前的问题，也就是关于人择原理的。我认为我们年底前能够达到 5 吉瓦左右，也许会更多一点，通过他们自己以及他们的产品通过 Bedrock、Vertex 或 Foundry 提供服务。我认为他们能达到五到六吉瓦，这远高于他们最初的计划，对吧？反正，大概就是这样，OpenAI 也差不多，可能更高一点，实际上根据我们的数据来看，还要高一点。话说回来，GPU 的折旧周期是多久？
(12:02)
Michael Burry was saying it's, you know, three years or less, right? It's like sort of his argument. And there's sort of two ways and lenses to look at this. Like mechanically, in this, you know, there's a TCO model, right? Total cost of ownership of a GPU, where we sort of project pricing out for GPUs and build up the total cost of a cluster. But there's a number of costs, right? There's your data center cost, right? There's your networking costs. There's your smart hands and people in the data center swapping stuff out. There's your spare parts, right? There's your actual chip cost. There's your server cost. All these various costs gets lumped together and there's some depreciation cycles on it.
Michael Burry 说，你知道，三年或更短，对吧？这就像是他的论点。对此，有两种方法和角度来看待。比如从机械角度来看，这里有一个 TCO 模型，对吧？GPU 的总拥有成本，我们据此预测 GPU 的价格，并计算出集群的总成本。但这里有很多成本，对吧？有数据中心的成本，对吧？有网络成本。还有智能运维人员在数据中心更换设备的成本。还有备件成本，对吧？还有实际的芯片成本。还有服务器成本。所有这些不同的成本加在一起，然后有一定的折旧周期。
(12:36)

还有一定的信贷成本。然后你就可以得出结论，好吧，这就是你如何计算出，如果你的折旧是五年，那么大规模部署 H100 在五年内的成本是每小时 1.40 美元。然后，如果你以每小时 2 美元的价格签订五年协议，那么你的毛利率大约是 35%。实际上略高于这个数字，但如果你以 1.90 美元的价格签约，那么毛利率大概是 35%。然后你假设到了第五年，GPU 就报废了，对吧？它坏了。而且在某些情况下，人们提出的论点是，如果你没有签署长期协议，因为英伟达每两年就会将性能提高三倍，
(13:11)
quadrupling the performance, while only 2x-ing the price or 50% increasing the price, Then the price of an H100, sure, maybe the value in the market was  1 an hour. Actually, the hopper is only worth 70 cents an hour. And so the price of a GPU would continue to fall. That's like one lens.
性能翻两番，而价格只提高 2 倍或 50%，那么 H100 的价格，当然，也许 2024 年市场上它的价值是 2 美元，毛利率为 35%。但在 2026 年，当 Blackwell 大量上市，每年部署数百万个时，你实际上每小时只值 1 美元。如果 Rubin 在 27 年实现超高产量，即使今年开始出货，明年也会实现超高产量，每年数百万颗芯片部署到云端，性能提高 3 倍，价格降低 50% 甚至 2 倍。实际上，Hopper 每小时只值 70 美分。因此 GPU 的价格将继续下降。这就像一个视角。
(13:51)
The other lens is what is the utility you get out of the chip, right? Because if you could build infinite Rubin or infinite of the newest chip, then yes, that's exactly what would happen. The price of a hopper would fall at a spot or a short-term contract rate. As the new chips come out and the price per performance goes up, but because you are so limited on semiconductors and deployment timelines and all these things, you end up with actually what prices these chips is not, hey, what's the comparative thing I can buy today? It's actually what is the value I can derive out of this chip today, right?
另一个视角是，你从芯片中获得的效用是什么？因为如果你能制造无限的 Rubin 或最新的芯片，那么是的，这正是会发生的情况。Hopper 的价格将会按照即期或短期合同价下跌。随着新芯片的推出，每单位性能的价格会上涨，但由于你在半导体和部署时间表以及所有这些方面都受到限制，最终决定这些芯片价格的实际上不是，嘿，我今天能买到的同类产品是什么？而是我今天能从这块芯片中获得什么价值，对吧？
(14:26)
And in that sense, Let's take GPT 5.4. GPT 5.4 is both way cheaper to run than GPT 4, has fewer active parameters. It's much smaller, right, in that sense of active parameters, plus because, you know, a sparser MOE versus GPT 4 being a coarser MOE. There's also been so many other advancements in training, RL, model architecture, et cetera, et cetera, data qualities. All these things that have made GPT-5.4 way better than GPT-4 and it's cheaper to serve. And so when you look at an H100, it can serve more tokens per GPU of 5.4 than if you had ran GPT-4 on it, right? So at some sense, it's producing more tokens of a model that is of higher quality.
从这个意义上说，我们来看看 GPT 5.4。GPT 5.4 的运行成本比 GPT 4 低得多，而且活跃参数更少。它小得多，对吧，就活跃参数而言，而且，你知道，它是更稀疏的 MOE，而 GPT 4 是更粗糙的 MOE。在训练、强化学习、模型架构以及数据质量等方面也取得了许多其他进展。所有这些都使得 GPT-5.4 比 GPT-4 更好，而且服务成本更低。因此，当你观察 H100 时，它在每个 GPU 上可以服务的 5.4 tokens 比你在其上运行 GPT-4 时更多，对吧？所以从某种意义上说，它产生了更高质量模型的更多 tokens。
(15:10)
In some sense, obviously, GPT-4, what is the maximum TAM for its tokens? Maybe it was a few billion dollars, maybe it was tens of billions of dollars. Adoption takes time. For GPT-5.4, that number is probably north of 100 billion, but there's an adoption lag and there's competition, so other people are getting it. And there's the constant improvements that everyone else is having. So if improvements stopped here, the value of an H100 is now predicated on the value that GPT-5.4 can get out of it instead of the value that GPT-4 can get out of it. And the margins and all that stuff that these labs are doing and they're in a competitive environment, so their margins can't go to infinity.
在某种程度上，显然，GPT-4 的 tokens 的最大 TAM 是多少？也许是几十亿美元，也许是数百亿美元。普及需要时间。对于 GPT-5.4 来说，这个数字可能超过 1000 亿美元，但存在普及滞后和竞争，所以其他人也在获得它。而且每个人都在不断改进。因此，如果改进停在这里，H100 的价值现在取决于 GPT-5.4 可以从中获得的价值，而不是 GPT-4 可以从中获得的价值。这些实验室正在做的利润和所有这些东西，而且它们处于竞争激烈的环境中，所以它们的利润不可能无限增长。
(15:44)
So you sort of have this like dynamic that is quite interesting in that. And H100 is worth more today than it was three years ago.
所以你在某种程度上拥有这种非常有趣的动态。现在 H100 比三年前更有价值。

The Elkin-Allen Effect and the Value of Long-Term Compute Contracts
Elkin-Allen 效应和长期计算合同的价值
Dwarkesh introduces the Elkin-Allen effect, explaining that increasing the fixed cost of goods can push consumers to choose higher-quality options. He wonders if this applies to AI, suggesting that more expensive GPUs might lead people to pay higher margins for slightly better models. Dylan agrees, noting that the price differential between models decreases as GPU prices increase. He adds that companies with long-term compute contracts have a margin advantage.
Dwarkesh 介绍了 Elkin-Allen 效应，解释说增加商品的固定成本可以促使消费者选择更高质量的选择。他想知道这是否适用于人工智能，并认为更昂贵的 GPU 可能会导致人们为稍微好一点的模型支付更高的利润率。Dylan 表示同意，并指出随着 GPU 价格上涨，模型之间的价格差异会缩小。他补充说，拥有长期计算合同的公司具有利润优势。
Dylan Patel:
(18:52)
Yeah, I think, you know, going back to like sort of the earlier view that if the models are so powerful, the value of a GPU goes up over time. As we approach closer and closer to, let's say, a point where right now only OpenAI and Anthropic have that viewpoint. As we approach further and further out, actually everyone is going to, even with open source models, be able to start to see that value skyrocket per GPU. In that sense, you should commit now to compute. Interestingly, in like an anthropic fashion, right? You know, there's a bit of a meme that they have problems with commitment issues and they're like sort of polyamorous. Not Dardario, but this is a bit of a meme.
是的，我认为，你知道，回到早期的观点，如果模型非常强大，那么 GPU 的价值会随着时间的推移而上升。当我们越来越接近，比如说，现在只有 OpenAI 和 Anthropic 持有这种观点的时候。随着我们越来越接近，实际上每个人都将能够，即使是使用开源模型，也能开始看到每个 GPU 的价值飙升。从这个意义上说，你应该立即投入计算。有趣的是，就像 Anthropic 的风格一样，对吧？你知道，有一种说法是他们有承诺问题，而且他们有点像多角恋。不是 Dardario，但这只是一个玩笑。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(19:39)
This explains everything. By the way, so there's this interesting economics effect called Elkin-Allen, which is the idea that if you increase The fixed cost of different goods, one of which is higher quality and one which is lower quality. That will make people choose the higher quality good on the margin. So to give a specific example, suppose the, you know, better tasting apple costs  1. Okay, now suppose you put an import tariff on them. And so now it's  2 for like great apple, medium apple, right?
这解释了一切。顺便说一下，有一种有趣的经济学效应叫做 Elkin-Allen 效应，它的观点是，如果你增加不同商品的固定成本，其中一种质量较高，另一种质量较低。这将使人们在边际上选择质量更高的商品。举个具体的例子，假设，你知道，味道更好的苹果售价 2 美元，而质量较差的苹果售价 1 美元。好的，现在假设你对它们征收进口关税。那么现在优质苹果的价格是 3 美元，普通苹果的价格是 2 美元，对吧？
Dylan Patel:
(20:15)
Is that because they both increased by a dollar or should it be like 50% increase?
这是因为它们都增加了一美元，还是应该像增加 50% 那样？
Dwarkesh Patel:
(20:18)
No, no, because if they both increased by a dollar, the whole effect is that if there's a fixed cost that's applied to both, The price difference between them, the ratio changes. So previously it was like the more expensive one was 2x more expensive. Now it's just 1.5x more expensive. So I wonder if applied to AI, that would mean that, look, if GPUs are going to get more expensive, there will be a fixed cost increase in the price of compute. As a result, that will push people to be willing to pay higher margins for slightly better models. Because the calculus is I'm going to be paying all this money for the compute anyways.
不，不，因为如果它们都增加了一美元，整个效应是，如果对两者都适用固定成本，它们之间的价格差异，即比率会发生变化。之前，更贵的那个是便宜的那个的两倍。现在只是 1.5 倍。所以我想知道如果应用于人工智能，那是否意味着，如果 GPU 的价格会上涨，计算价格的固定成本将会增加。因此，这将促使人们愿意为稍微好一点的模型支付更高的利润。因为计算方法是，无论如何我都要为计算支付所有这些钱。
(20:55)
I might as well just pay slightly more to making sure it's like the very best model rather than a model that's slightly worse.
我不妨多花一点钱，确保它是最好的模型，而不是稍微差一点的模型。

Cloud Player Pricing, Margin Accrual, and the Model Vendor Landscape
云玩家定价、利润累积和模型供应商格局
Dylan explains that in a compute-limited world, companies with long-term contracts have a margin advantage. He discusses how cloud players like CoreWeave have long-term contracts, limiting their ability to flex pricing. The incremental added compute is where all the cost is. He identifies potential margin holders as cloud players, chip vendors, and memory vendors, while model vendors may see margins increase this year due to capacity constraints.
Dylan 解释说，在计算能力有限的世界中，拥有长期合同的公司具有利润优势。他讨论了 CoreWeave 等云玩家如何拥有长期合同，从而限制了他们灵活定价的能力。增量增加的计算就是所有成本所在。他认为潜在的利润持有者是云玩家、芯片供应商和内存供应商，而由于容量限制，模型供应商可能会在今年看到利润增长。
Dylan Patel:
(21:01)
Right. So the Hopper went from two to three dollars. And if the Hopper can make a million tokens of Opus and it can make two million tokens of Sonnet, the price differential between Opus and Sonnet has decreased because the price of the GPU has increased by a dollar from two to three. Interesting. I think that makes a ton of sense. Also, I think we just see all of the volumes are on the best models today, all the revenues on the best models today. And in a compute limited world, there's sort of two things that happen, right? A, companies that have locked up, you know, and don't have commitment issues, you know, have these five year contracts for compute.
对。所以 Hopper 从 2 美元涨到了 3 美元。如果 Hopper 可以生成一百万个 Opus 代币，并且可以生成两百万个 Sonnet 代币，那么 Opus 和 Sonnet 之间的价格差异已经缩小，因为 GPU 的价格从 2 美元上涨到 3 美元。有意思。我认为这很有道理。此外，我认为我们现在看到的所有销量都在最好的模型上，现在的所有收入都在最好的模型上。在一个计算资源有限的世界里，会发生两件事，对吧？第一，那些已经锁定，你知道，没有承诺问题的公司，拥有这些为期五年的计算合同。
(21:41)
They've kind of locked in a humongous margin advantage because they've locked in compute for five years at a price of what it transacted at five years ago or three years ago or two years ago, whatever it is. Whereas if you're now three years into that five-year contract and someone else's two-year contract or three-year contract rolled off, and now you're trying to buy that at modern pricing, when you're priced to the value of models, the price is going to be up a lot more. And so in a sense, the person who committed Early has better margins in general.
他们已经锁定了一个巨大的利润优势，因为他们以五年前、三年前或两年前的价格锁定了五年的计算资源，无论是什么时候。然而，如果你现在已经进入五年合同的第三年，而其他人的两年合同或三年合同已经到期，而你现在正试图以现代价格购买，当你按照模型的价值定价时，价格会上涨很多。所以从某种意义上说，早期承诺的人通常有更好的利润。
(22:11)
And the percentage of the market that is in long term contracts is much larger than the percentage of the market in short term contracts that can be this sort of flex capacity that you add at the last second. And at the same time, right? So where does the margin go, right? Because models get more valuable. How much can the cloud players flex their pricing? Well, if in fact, like if you look at CoreWeave, their average term duration is like over three years right now. And for like 98% plus of their compute, it's over three years. And so they end up with this like conundrum of like, well, they can't actually flex price.

NVIDIA's Strategy and TSMC's Allocation of 3nm Capacity
NVIDIA 的战略和台积电的 3 纳米产能分配
Dwarkesh and Dylan discuss NVIDIA's strategy of fracturing complementary industries to maximize leverage, contrasting it with TSMC's allocation of 3nm capacity. Dylan explains that TSMC is providing good allocations to companies doing CPUs, like Amazon and AMD, because they view the CPU business as more stable and long-term. He notes that NVIDIA is getting the majority of 3nm supply because they signaled demand earlier and more aggressively than Google or Amazon.
Dwarkesh 和 Dylan 讨论了 NVIDIA 通过分裂互补行业以最大限度地提高杠杆作用的战略，并将其与台积电的 3 纳米产能分配进行了对比。Dylan 解释说，台积电正在为从事 CPU 业务的公司（如亚马逊和 AMD）提供良好的分配，因为他们认为 CPU 业务更稳定和长期。他指出，NVIDIA 获得了大部分 3 纳米供应，因为他们比谷歌或亚马逊更早、更积极地发出了需求信号。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(24:51)
Yeah, let's get into logic and memory. How specifically NVIDIA has been able to lock up so much of both? So if you, I think, according to your numbers, by 27, NVIDIA is going to have like 70 plus percent of N3 wafer capacity or something like that, or around that area. And then I forget what the numbers were for memory at SK Hynix and Samsung and so forth. But if you look at, so think about how the NeoCloud business works and how NVIDIA works with that, or how the RL environment business works and how Anthropic works with that. 好的，我们来谈谈逻辑和内存。具体来说，英伟达是如何锁定如此多的逻辑和内存的？所以，如果你，我认为，根据你们的数据，到 27 年，英伟达将拥有 N3 晶圆产能的 70% 以上，或者类似比例，或接近那个范围。然后我忘了 SK 海力士和三星等公司的内存数据是多少了。但如果你看看，想想 NeoCloud 业务是如何运作的，以及英伟达是如何与它合作的，或者 RL 环境业务是如何运作的，以及 Anthropic 是如何与它合作的。在这两种情况下，英伟达都在故意破坏互补产业，以确保他们拥有尽可能多的 leverage。

TSMC's Market Signals and NVIDIA's AGI-Pilled Approach
台积电的市场信号和英伟达的 AGI 信仰策略
Dylan explains that TSMC relies on market signals, such as non-cancelable orders and deposits, to forecast demand. NVIDIA acted earlier than Google and Amazon, securing more capacity. TSMC checks with PCB and memory vendors to ensure sufficient capacity. NVIDIA, while not fully "AGI-pilled," was more so than Google or Amazon in Q3 of last year. Google, despite having better TPUs, has to deploy GPUs to fill data centers due to TPU supply constraints.
Dylan 解释说，台积电依靠市场信号（如不可取消的订单和定金）来预测需求。 英伟达比谷歌和亚马逊更早采取行动，确保了更多产能。 台积电会与 PCB 和内存供应商核实，以确保有足够的产能。 英伟达虽然没有完全 “AGI 信仰化”，但在去年第三季度比谷歌或亚马逊更甚。 谷歌虽然拥有更好的 TPU，但由于 TPU 供应受限，不得不部署 GPU 来填补数据中心。
Dylan Patel:
(26:07)
Yeah, so I think There's a couple points here. On 3nm, if we go back to last year, the vast majority of 3nm was Apple. Apple is being moved to 2nm. Memory prices are going up, so Apple's volumes may go down because as memory prices go up, either they cut margin or they move on. There's some time lag because they have long-term contracts. But basically, Apple likely reduces demand slash moves to two nanometer faster, where two nanometer is only capable of a sort of mobile chips today. And in the future, AI chips will move there. So sort of Apple has that. And then Apple is also talking to third party vendors because they're getting squeezed out of TSMC a little bit.

(27:29)
And As a company that is conservative and doesn't want to ride cycles of growth too hard, you actually want to allocate to the market that is more stable and lower growth rate first before you allocate all the incremental capacity to the fast growth rate market. That is the case generally. And so when you look at like, hey, same for AMD, right? The allocations they get on their CPUs is like, TSMC is much more excited about those than they are for GPUs. By and large, most of these things will be on three nanometer by the end of this year with the Rubin launch and all the chips that are in that family,
作为一家保守的公司，不想过度追逐增长周期，你实际上希望首先将产能分配给更稳定、增长率更低的市场，然后再将所有增量产能分配给快速增长的市场。一般情况都是这样。所以当你看到，比如，AMD 也是一样，对吧？他们在 CPU 上获得的分配是，台积电对这些比对 GPU 更感兴趣。亚马逊也是如此。英伟达有点独特，因为是的，他们有 CPU。是的，他们生产交换机。是的，他们生产网络设备。他们生产 NVLink。他们生产所有这些不同的产品，InfiniBand，以太网，所有这些不同的产品，网卡。总的来说，这些产品中的大多数将在今年年底随着 Rubin 的发布以及该系列中的所有芯片采用三纳米制程，

Google's TPU Sales to Anthropic and Subsequent AGI Awakening
谷歌向 Anthropic 出售 TPU 以及随后的 AGI 觉醒
Dwarkesh questions why Google sold TPUs to Anthropic instead of giving them to DeepMind. Dylan explains that Anthropic's compute team, formerly of Google, negotiated the deal before Google fully realized the potential of AI. Google then had to request increased capacity from TSMC. Google's leadership woke up after seeing user metrics skyrocket with Nano, Banana, and Gemini 3, leading them to become "absurdly AGI-pilled" and invest heavily in data centers and power.
Dwarkesh 问，为什么谷歌将 TPU 出售给 Anthropic，而不是给 DeepMind。 Dylan 解释说，Anthropic 的计算团队（前谷歌员工）在谷歌完全意识到 AI 的潜力之前就达成了这笔交易。 谷歌随后不得不要求台积电增加产能。 谷歌的领导层在看到 Nano、Banana 和 Gemini 3 的用户指标飙升后醒悟过来，这导致他们变得 “非常 AGI 信仰化”，并大量投资于数据中心和电力。
Dylan Patel:
(30:05)

ASML's EUV Tools: The Ultimate Bottleneck for AI Compute Scaling
ASML 的 EUV 工具：AI 计算扩展的终极瓶颈
Dylan states that by 2028-2029, the bottleneck falls to ASML, the maker of EUV tools. ASML can only produce a limited number of these tools per year, capping the potential for AI compute scaling. He calculates that a gigawatt of NVIDIA's Rubin chips requires 3.5 EUV tools, highlighting the disproportionate impact of this limited tooling on the entire AI supply chain.
Dylan 表示，到 2028-2029 年，瓶颈将落在 EUV 工具制造商 ASML 身上。 ASML 每年只能生产数量有限的这些工具，从而限制了 AI 计算扩展的潜力。 他计算得出，1 吉瓦英伟达 Rubin 芯片需要 3.5 个 EUV 工具，这突显了这种有限的工具对整个 AI 供应链的巨大影响。

EUV Tool Capacity and ASML's Generosity
EUV 工具产能和 ASML 的慷慨
Dylan says that Sam Altman's goal is completely compatible, as there will be around 700 EUV tools by the end of the decade, enough for 200 gigawatts of AI chips. He notes that ASML has been shipping EUV tools for a decade, but only entered mass volume production around 2020. He also says that ASML is maybe one of the most generous companies in the world.
Dylan 说，Sam Altman 的目标是完全相符的，因为到本十年末将有大约 700 台 EUV 工具，足以生产 200 吉瓦的 AI 芯片。 他指出，ASML 已经交付 EUV 工具十年了，但大约在 2020 年才进入批量生产阶段。 他还说，ASML 可能是世界上最慷慨的公司之一。
Dylan Patel:
(42:16)
Right. That's completely compatible, right? Because if you think about TSMC and the entire ecosystem has something 250 to 300 EUV tools already. And then you stack on 70 this year, 80 next year, growing to 100 by 2030. You're at like 700 EUV tools by the end of the decade. 700 EUV tools, three and a half tools per gigawatt. He explains that ASML's tool has four major components, each with tremendously complex supply chains that have not tried to expand massively. He says that Nvidia is building X minus one and you go down the supply chain, everyone's doing minus one.
Dwarkesh 问，如果 ASML 决定将其资本支出增加一倍或两倍，会发生什么情况。 Dylan 说，ASML 并没有决定直接 YOLO，让我们尽快扩大产能。 他解释说，ASML 的工具包含四个主要组件，每个组件都有极其复杂的供应链，而这些供应链并没有试图大规模扩张。 他说，英伟达正在构建 X 减 1，而当你沿着供应链向下走时，每个人都在做减 1。

The Performance Difference Between A100 and Blackwell

He says that the performance difference is not just going to be the difference in flops.

Dylan Patel:
(57:54)
Yeah, so I think, you know, we potentially do go crazy enough that this is, this happens because we just need incremental compute and the compute is worth the higher cost, power, etc. of these chips. Often, it's easy to boil things down to flops per watt or flops per dollar. But that's actually not a fair comparison, right?

(59:28)
And so this is where sort of you can bring in, hey, let's look at Kimi K1 or DeepSeq. And Most of this is not attributed to flops or numerics, right? Because those models are actually 8-bit. So it's not like Blackwell's and Hopper, they're both optimized for 8-bit and Blackwell's not really taking advantage of its 4-bit there. The performance gulf is actually much larger. And the way you can sort of compare them and think about them is, sure, it's one thing to shrink process technology and make the transistor smaller and each chip has X number of flops.
所以在这里你可以引入，嘿，让我们看看 Kimi K1 或 DeepSeq。当你看到 Kimi 或 Kimi K2.5（抱歉）和 DeepSeq，当你看到这两个模型，以及它们在 Hopper 与 Blackwell 上的表现时，你知道，在非常优化的软件上，你会得到截然不同的性能，对吧？而且这大部分并非归因于 flops 或数值，对吧？因为这些模型实际上是 8 位的。所以不是像 Blackwell 和 Hopper 那样，它们都针对 8 位进行了优化，而 Blackwell 并没有真正利用它的 4 位优势。性能差距实际上要大得多。你可以比较和思考它们的方式是，当然，缩小工艺技术，使晶体管更小，每个芯片都有 X 个 flops，这是一回事。
(1:00:16)
But you forget the big gating factors is that these models don't run on a single chip. They run on Hundreds of chips at a time, right? If you look at DeepSeq's production deployment, which is well over a year old now, they were running on 160 GPUs, right? And that's what they serve production traffic on. And so they split the model across 160 GPUs. Every time you cross the barrier of a chip to another chip, there is an efficiency loss because you now have to transmit over, you know, high-speed electrical surties, and there is a latency cost, there's a power cost, there's all these dynamics that hurt.
但你忘记了一个重要的限制因素，即这些模型并非在单个芯片上运行。它们一次在数百个芯片上运行，对吧？如果你看看 DeepSeq 的生产部署，它已经有一年多的历史了，它们在 160 个 GPU 上运行，对吧？这就是他们提供生产流量的方式。因此，他们将模型拆分到 160 个 GPU 上。每次你跨越一个芯片到另一个芯片的障碍时，都会有效率损失，因为你现在必须通过传输，你知道，高速电路，而且存在延迟成本，存在功耗成本，存在所有这些不利因素。
(1:00:47)
As you shrink and shrink and shrink the process node, Increase the amount of compute in a single chip. Now, in chip, right, movement of data is, you know, at hundreds or of at least tens of terabytes a second, if not hundreds of terabytes a second. Whereas between chips, you're on the order of a terabytes of second, right? And so this movement of data between chips that are super close to each other physically, and then you can only put so many chips close to each other physically. So you have to put chips in different racks. The order of data between that is on the order of hundreds of gigabits a second, right? 400 gig or 800 gig a second. So 100 gigabytes a second, roughly.
随着你不断缩小工艺节点，增加单个芯片中的计算量。现在，在芯片中，数据的移动速度是每秒数百或至少数十 TB，如果不是每秒数百 TB 的话。而在芯片之间，速度约为每秒 TB 级别，对吧？因此，这种在彼此物理距离非常近的芯片之间的数据移动，而且你只能将这么多芯片彼此物理距离如此近。所以你必须将芯片放在不同的机架中。它们之间的数据顺序约为每秒数百 Gb，对吧？400 Gb 或 800 Gb 每秒。大约是每秒 100 GB。
(1:01:27)
And so you've got this like huge ladder of like, oh, on chip, I can communicate at super fast speeds. Within the rack, I can communicate at order of magnitude speeds. Outside the rack, I can communicate at an even order of magnitude lower than that. And as you break the bounds of chips, You end up with this performance loss. So anyways, the reason I explain this is because when you look at Hopper versus Blackwell, even if both of them are using a rack worth of chips, the Hopper is significantly slower because the amount of performance that you have Leverage to the task within that, you know, within each domain of, hey, tens of terabytes of seconds of communication between these transistors or these processing elements.
因此，你就有了这样一个巨大的阶梯，比如，哦，在芯片上，我可以以超快的速度进行通信。在机架内，我可以以数量级的速度进行通信。在机架外，我可以以比这更低的量级进行通信。当你打破芯片的界限时，最终会导致性能损失。所以，我解释这个的原因是，当你比较 Hopper 和 Blackwell 时，即使它们都使用一个机架的芯片，Hopper 的速度也明显较慢，因为你对任务的性能利用程度，你知道，在每个领域内，这些晶体管或处理元件之间存在着数十 TB/秒的通信。
(1:02:04)
And, you know, terabytes a second between these processing elements is much, much higher, and therefore the performance is much higher. So when you look at inference at, let's say, 100 tokens a second for DeepSeq and KimiK 2.5, Hopper versus Blackwell, the performance difference is on the order of 20x.
而且，你知道，这些处理单元之间的速度高达每秒数 TB，因此性能要高得多。所以，当你看到 DeepSeq 和 KimiK 2.5，Hopper 和 Blackwell 在每秒 100 个 token 的推理速度时，性能差异大约在 20 倍左右。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(1:02:21)
Interesting.
有意思。

Scaling the Number of Chips and the Future of Packaging
扩展芯片数量和封装的未来
Dwarkesh asks what is preventing us from just doing that with How many dyes could you have a single chip and still get these tens of terabytes a second. Dylan says that even within Blackwell, there are differences in performance when you're communicating on the chip versus across the chips. He says that you will see a trend line of more chips on the package.
Dwarkesh 问，是什么阻止我们这样做，即在单个芯片上可以有多少个芯片，并且仍然可以获得每秒数十 TB 的速度。 Dylan 说，即使在 Blackwell 内部，当你在芯片上进行通信时，与在芯片之间进行通信时，性能也存在差异。 他说，你会看到封装上芯片数量增加的趋势线。
Dylan Patel:
(1:02:21)
Not 2 or 3x like the flops, Performance difference indicates, even though those are on the same process node, there's just differences in networking technologies and what they've worked on. And so you can translate some of these back. But when you look at like Rubin, what they're doing on three nanometers, some of these things are just not possible to do all the way back on A100, even if you make a new chip for seven nanometer. There's just like certain architectural improvements you can port. There's certain ones you cannot. And so the performance difference is not just going to be the difference in flops. It's in some senses, cumulative between the difference in, you know, flops per chip, networking speed between chips, how many flops are on a chip versus a system,
不是像 flops 那样的 2 或 3 倍。性能差异表明，即使它们在同一个制程节点上，只是在网络技术和他们所做的工作上存在差异。所以你可以把其中一些转换回来。但是当你看到像 Rubin 这样的，他们在 3 纳米上所做的事情，有些事情是不可能在 A100 上完全实现的，即使你为 7 纳米制造一个新的芯片。有些架构上的改进是可以移植的。有些则不行。所以性能差异不仅仅是 flops 上的差异。在某种意义上，它是芯片的 flops 差异、芯片间的网络速度、一个芯片与一个系统上的 flops 数量之间的累积效应，
(1:02:59)
memory bandwidth on a single chip and on an entire system. All of these things compound.
单个芯片和整个系统上的内存带宽。所有这些因素都会叠加。

是的，所以即使在 Blackwell 内部，在芯片上通信和跨芯片通信时，性能也存在差异。这些界限显然比你离开整个芯片时要小得多，但每个 die 与封装内部的通信也存在差异。所以无论如何，当你扩大芯片数量时，都会有一些性能损失。这不是完美的，但它比不同的整个封装要好得多。现在，先进封装可以扩展到多大？英伟达的做法是 CoOS，谷歌、博通、联发科和亚马逊的做法，Tranium，所有这些芯片都在做的是 CoOS。但实际上你可以回顾一下特斯拉用 Dojo 做的事情，对吧？

Dojo, which they canceled and restarted. Anyways, Dojo was a chip that was the size of an entire wafer. They had 25 chips on it. And there were some trade-offs, right? They couldn't put HBM on it. But the positive side of it was that they had 25 chips on it. And so to date, it is still probably the best chip for running convolutional neural networks. Dojo，他们取消并重新启动了。无论如何，Dojo 是一个像整个晶圆一样大的芯片。上面有 25 个芯片。并且存在一些权衡，对吧？他们无法在上面放置 HBM。但它的积极之处在于它有 25 个芯片。所以到目前为止，它可能仍然是运行卷积神经网络的最佳芯片。只是它不太擅长 transformers，因为你知道，芯片的形状，内存、算术，所有这些规格都不太适合 transformers。它们非常适合 CNN。无论如何，你知道，Dojo 芯片是围绕这一点优化的。
(1:04:51)

那么，这就相当于大约 130 亿到 140 亿美元的计算成本，以租赁成本计算，实际上相当于某人为 Anthropic 投入了价值 500 亿美元的资本支出，以产生他们当前的收入。而中国还没有做到这一点。如果 Anthropic 的收入再次增长 10 倍，而且我认为答案是 “何时” 而不是 “是否”，那么中国就没有足够的计算能力来进行如此大规模的部署。所以在某种程度上，感觉就像，哦，我们正处于快速起飞的状态，对吧？这不像我们谈论的是在某个日期之前建成戴森球。更像是收入以如此快的速度复合增长，以至于它确实会影响经济增长。

Bandwidth Constraints and the Performance of HBM
带宽限制和 HBM 的性能
Dylan says that you're still limited, you know, one of the like core constraints of chips, even though they're, you know, sort of like, you know, a chip is like a certain size, all of the IO escapes on the edges of the chip. He says that the metric that you actually care about is bandwidth per wafer, not bits per wafer. He says that if you switch to DDR, yes, you produce 4x the bits, per DRAM wafer, but all of a sudden the constraints shift a lot and your system design shifts a lot.
Dylan 说，你仍然受到限制，你知道，芯片的核心约束之一，即使它们，你知道，有点像，你知道，芯片有一定的尺寸，所有的 IO 都从芯片的边缘逸出。他说，你真正关心的指标是每晶圆的带宽，而不是每晶圆的比特数。他说，如果你切换到 DDR，是的，你每 DRAM 晶圆的产量是 4 倍，但突然之间，约束条件发生了很大变化，你的系统设计也发生了很大变化。
Dylan Patel:
(1:17:16)

(1:17:54)
like the curve on inference throughput versus speed is there already just on HBM. And yet they don't, because no one actually wants to use a slow model. (1:18:35)
But then there's a couple like things that are challenging with this, right? You could use regular DRAM. One is you're still limited, you know, one of the like core constraints of chips, even though they're, you know, sort of like, you know, a chip is like a certain size, all of the IO escapes on the edges of the chip, right? So oftentimes, you know, what you see is the left and the right of the chip are HBM, the IO from the chip to the HBM is on the sides and then the top and bottom are IO to other chips, right? And so if you were to change from HBM to DDR, then all of a sudden this IO on this edge would have significantly less bandwidth, but it had significantly more capacity per chip.
但这里有一些具有挑战性的事情，对吧？你可以使用普通的 DRAM。一是你仍然受到限制，你知道，芯片的核心约束之一，即使它们，你知道，有点像，你知道，芯片有一定的尺寸，所有的 IO 都从芯片的边缘逸出，对吧？所以通常，你知道，你看到的是芯片的左侧和右侧是 HBM，从芯片到 HBM 的 IO 在两侧，然后顶部和底部是到其他芯片的 IO，对吧？所以，如果你要从 HBM 更改为 DDR，那么突然间，此边缘上的 IO 的带宽将大大降低，但每个芯片的容量却大大增加。
(1:19:20)
And so yes, you're making less You know, the metric that you actually care about is bandwidth per wafer, not bits per wafer.
所以，是的，你正在减少，你知道，你真正关心的指标是每片晶圆的带宽，而不是每片晶圆的比特数。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(1:19:30)
Because the thing that is constraining the flops is just getting in and out the next matrix, and for that you just need more bandwidth.
因为限制浮点运算的事情只是进出下一个矩阵，为此你只需要更多的带宽。
Dylan Patel:
(1:19:39)

是的，取出权重并进出 KV 缓存。
Dwarkesh Patel:

Dylan Patel:
(1:19:43)
