How much do I offload to other chips and call when I need it for tool calling or whatever? How much do I, how many chips do I paralyze this on? Obviously these are like, the search space of this is like very broad, which is why we have like inference X, like this is like an open source model, like searches all the optimal points on inference for a variety of eight different chips The point is, you're not always necessarily constrained by memory capacity.
在许多情况下，这些 GPU 并没有以全部内存容量运行。是的，这显然像是一个系统设计的事情，你知道，模型硬件、软件协同设计，嘿，我做多少 KVCache 呢？我要在芯片上保留多少？我要卸载到其他芯片多少，并在需要工具调用或其他操作时调用它们？我要并行处理多少芯片？显然，搜索空间非常广泛，所以我们有推理 X，这是一个开源模型，在推理中搜索各种不同芯片上的所有最佳点。关键是，你不一定总是受内存容量的限制。

The Bandwidth Difference Between HBM and Normal DRAM
HBM 和普通 DRAM 之间的带宽差异
Dwarkesh asks what is the bandwidth difference between HBM and a normal DRAM. Dylan says that an HBM stack of HBM4 is 2048 bits on an area that's 13 millimeters wide. He says that there's an order of magnitude difference in bandwidth per edge area. He says that if it takes 4X more wafer area to get the same byte for HBM, you had to destroy 4X as much consumer demand for laptops and phones and whatever in order to free up one byte for AI.
Dwarkesh 问，HBM 和普通 DRAM 之间的带宽差异是多少。Dylan 说，一个 HBM4 的 HBM 堆栈在 13 毫米宽的区域上有 2048 位。他说，每边缘区域的带宽存在一个数量级的差异。他说，如果获得相同的 HBM 字节需要 4 倍的晶圆面积，那么你必须摧毁 4 倍的笔记本电脑和手机等的消费者需求，才能为 AI 腾出一个字节。
Dylan Patel:
(1:20:22)
You can be constrained by flops, you can be constrained by network bandwidth, you can be constrained by memory bandwidth, or you can be constrained by memory capacity. If you're really to simplify it down, there's like four constraints, and each of these can break out into more. But in this case, if you switch to DDR, yes, you produce 4x the bits, per DRAM wafer, but all of a sudden the constraints shift a lot and your system design shifts a lot. You go slower. Yes. Is the market smaller? Okay, maybe possibly, but also now all of a sudden all these flops are wasted because they're just sitting there waiting for memory. It's like great.
你可能会受到浮点运算的限制，可能会受到网络带宽的限制，可能会受到内存带宽的限制，或者可能会受到内存容量的限制。如果真的要简化一下，大概有四个限制，而且每一个限制都可以分解成更多。但在这种情况下，如果你切换到 DDR，是的，每个 DRAM 晶圆产生的比特数是原来的 4 倍，但突然之间，限制条件发生很大变化，你的系统设计也会发生很大变化。你会变慢。是的。市场变小了吗？好吧，也许可能，但现在突然之间，所有的浮点运算都被浪费了，因为它们只是坐在那里等待内存。真是太好了。
(1:20:53)
I don't need all that capacity because I can't really increase batch size because then the KV cache is going to take even longer to read. And so you never, you can. Yeah.
我不需要那么多容量，因为我无法真正增加批量大小，因为这样 KV 缓存的读取时间会更长。所以你永远，你可以。是的。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(1:21:02)
Interesting. What is the bandwidth difference between HBM and a normal DRAM?
有意思。HBM 和普通 DRAM 之间的带宽差异是多少？
Dylan Patel:
(1:21:07)
Yeah, so an HBM stack of HBM4, let's just talk about like the stuff that's in Rubin because that's what we've been indexing on, is 2048 bits across connected in an area that's like 13 millimeters wide. So 2048 bits and it transfers memory at around 10 gigatransfers a second. So, a stack of HBM4 is 2048 bits on an area that's 13 millimeters wide, roughly, or 11. And that's the shoreline that you're taking on the chip. And in that shoreline, you have 2048 bits transferring at 10 gigatransfers per second. You multiply those together and you divide by 8 bits to bytes. You're at roughly 2.5 terabytes a second per HBM stack. When you look at DDR, in that same area, it's maybe 64 or 128 bits wide.
是的，所以一个 HBM4 堆栈，我们只讨论 Rubin 里面的东西，因为我们一直在关注它，在 13 毫米宽的区域内连接了 2048 位。因此，2048 位，它以大约每秒 10 千兆传输的速度传输内存。因此，HBM4 堆栈在 13 毫米宽（大致）或 11 毫米的区域上有 2048 位。这是你在芯片上占据的岸线。在这条岸线上，你有 2048 位以每秒 10 千兆传输的速度传输。你把它们乘起来，然后除以 8 位转换为字节。你大约是每个 HBM 堆栈每秒 2.5 TB。当你看 DDR 时，在同一区域，它可能只有 64 或 128 位宽。
(1:21:53)
And that DDR5 is transferring at anywhere from 6.4 gigatransfers a second to maybe 8,000 gigatransfers a second. So your bandwidth is significantly lower. It's 64 times 8,000 divided by 8. You're at 64 gigabytes a second. And even if you take a generous interpretation of 128 times 8 gigatransfers, you're at 128 gigabytes a second for the same shoreline versus two and a half terabytes a second. There's an order of magnitude difference in bandwidth per edge area. And if your chip is a square or it's 26 by 33, right, is the maximum size for a chip, individual die, you only have so much edge area. And then on the inside of that chip, you put all your compute.
而 DDR5 的传输速度从每秒 6.4 千兆传输到大约每秒 8000 千兆传输。所以你的带宽明显更低。它是 64 乘以 8,000 除以 8。你每秒是 64 GB。即使你对 128 乘以 8 千兆传输进行慷慨的解释，对于相同的岸线，你每秒也只有 128 GB，而 HBM 则是每秒 2.5 TB。每个边缘区域的带宽存在一个数量级的差异。如果你的芯片是正方形的，或者是 26 x 33，对吧，这是芯片、单个芯片的最大尺寸，你只有这么多的边缘区域。然后在芯片内部，你放置所有的计算。
(1:22:34)

有一些你可以尝试改变的事情，对吧？更多的 SRAM，更多的缓存，等等等等。但最终，你受到带宽的极大限制。

Dylan Patel:

NAND almost zero, but smartphones The percentage of NAND that goes to phones and PCs is larger than the percentage of DRAM that goes to phone and PC. So as you destroy demand, you unlock, you know, mostly for the DRAM purposes, you unlock more NAND that gets allocated and can sort of go to other markets.

A Total Disruption and the Use of New Technologies
一场彻底的颠覆和新技术的应用
Dwarkesh asks how surprised would you be if in 2030, people like there just happened to be some total disruption. Dylan says that something that's very simple and easy to scale, I have very, very low probability for. He says that there are a number of companies working on effectively like Particle accelerators or synchrotrons that generate light that's either 13.5 nanometer like EUV or even x-ray like even narrower wavelength like 7 nanometer or whatever wavelengths of light to then use in lithography tools.
Dwarkesh 问道，如果到 2030 年，突然发生某种彻底的颠覆，您会有多惊讶。Dylan 说，对于一些非常简单且易于扩展的事情，我认为发生的概率非常非常低。他说，现在有很多公司在研究粒子加速器或同步加速器，它们可以产生 13.5 纳米的 EUV 光，甚至像 X 射线一样，产生波长更窄的光，比如 7 纳米或其他波长的光，用于光刻工具。
Dylan Patel:
(1:33:26)
So I think, you know, as with any complex supply chain, it takes time and constraints shift over time. And even if something isn't any longer a constraint, that doesn't mean that market no longer has margin, right? So, for example, energy will not be a big bottleneck as we get to, you know, a couple of years from now. But that doesn't mean energy is not growing super fast and there's no margin there. It's just like it's not the key bottleneck. And in the space of fabs, right, clean rooms are the biggest bottleneck this year and next year. And as we get over time, 29, you know, 28, 29, 30, there will be still constraints there.
所以我认为，你知道，与任何复杂的供应链一样，都需要时间，并且约束会随着时间的推移而改变。即使某些东西不再是约束，也并不意味着该市场不再有利润，对吧？因此，例如，当我们达到几年后的水平时，能源将不再是一个大的瓶颈。但这并不意味着能源没有以超快的速度增长，并且那里没有利润。这只是它不是关键瓶颈。在晶圆厂领域，正确的，洁净室是今年和明年最大的瓶颈。随着时间的推移，29 年，你知道，28 年、29 年、30 年，仍然会有约束。
(1:33:57)
The thing about Elon is, I think he's had a tremendous capability to garner physical resources and really smart people to build things. 关于埃隆的事情是，我认为他有巨大的能力来获取物理资源和真正聪明的人来建造东西。他能够招募到真正了不起的人的方式就是尝试建造最疯狂的东西，对吧？在 AI 的案例中，这并没有真正奏效，因为每个人都在尝试构建 AGI。每个人都雄心勃勃。但如果我们打算去火星，制造能够自动着陆的火箭，或者制造完全自动驾驶的电动汽车，又或者制造辅助人类的机器人。

3D DRAM and the Retooling of Fabs
3D DRAM 和晶圆厂的改造
Dwarkesh asks in order to be able to build more memory in the future, could we build 3D DRAM the way we do 3D NAND and then go back to DUV. Dylan says that this is the hope. He says that everyone's roadmap for 3D DRAM is that you'll still use EUV because you want to have that tighter overlay because now when you're doing these subsequent processing steps, You want it to be, you know, everything's vertically stacked.
Dwarkesh 问道，为了将来能够构建更多的内存，我们是否可以像构建 3D NAND 一样构建 3D DRAM，然后再回到 DUV。Dylan 说这是希望。他说，每个人对于 3D DRAM 的规划都是继续使用 EUV，因为你希望拥有更紧密的重叠，因为现在当你在进行这些后续处理步骤时，你希望它是，你知道的，所有东西都是垂直堆叠的。
Dylan Patel:
(1:36:07)
Something that's very simple and easy to scale, I have very, very low probability for. There are a number of companies working on effectively like Particle accelerators or synchrotrons that generate light that's either 13.5 nanometer like EUV or even x-ray like even narrower wavelength like 7 nanometer or whatever wavelengths of light to then use in lithography tools. But those things are like massive particle accelerators that are then generating this light. It's a very complicated thing to build. So there's a couple companies and I think that that could be a big disruption to the industry beyond what EUV is.
对于那些非常简单且易于扩展的东西，我认为可能性非常非常低。有许多公司正在研究粒子加速器或同步加速器，它们产生的光要么是 13.5 纳米（如 EUV），要么甚至是 X 射线（如更窄波长的 7 纳米或用于光刻工具的任何波长的光）。但那些东西都是巨大的粒子加速器，用来产生这种光。建造起来非常复杂。所以有几家公司，我认为这可能会对行业产生重大颠覆，超越 EUV。
(1:36:38)
I don't necessarily think that like We're going to just magically build something new that is like direct write and super simple and can be manufactured at huge volumes, although there are some attempts to do things like this.
我不一定认为我们会神奇地创造出一种新的东西，比如直写式的、超级简单的、可以大量制造的东西，尽管有一些尝试这样做。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(1:36:50)
I ask because if you think about Elon Co's in the past, rocketry was this thing that was thought to be... I mean, it is incredibly complicated.
我问这个问题是因为，如果你想想埃隆公司过去的例子，火箭技术被认为是……我的意思是，它非常复杂。
Dylan Patel:
(1:36:58)

听着，与埃隆相比，我只是一个天真的饶舌者，对吧？我建造了什么？所以也许有可能，对吧？
Dwarkesh Patel:
(1:37:04)
Yeah. In order to be able to build more memory in the future, could we build 3D DRAM the way we do 3D NAND and then go back to DUV?
是的。为了将来能够制造更多的内存，我们能否像制造 3D NAND 一样制造 3D DRAM，然后再回到 DUV？
Dylan Patel:
(1:37:14)
This is the hope. Currently, everyone's roadmap for 3D DRAM is that you'll still use EUV because you want to have that tighter overlay because now when you're doing these subsequent processing steps, You want it to be, you know, everything's vertically stacked. You have more layers on top of each other. And you want the pitches to be tighter and all these things. So generally people are still trying to do an EUV, but what 3D would do is it would take the, you know, hey, a single EUV pass, how many bits can it make, right? If you do this sort of like calculation, and that number would go up drastically if you go to 3DDRAM. That is the hope.
这是希望。目前，每个人对 3D DRAM 的规划都是仍然使用 EUV，因为你希望有更严格的对准，因为现在当你进行这些后续处理步骤时，你希望它是，你知道，一切都是垂直堆叠的。你在彼此之上拥有更多的层。你希望间距更小，以及所有这些。所以一般来说，人们仍然在尝试使用 EUV，但 3D 可以实现的是，你知道，一次 EUV 通过可以制造多少比特？如果你做这种计算，如果你使用 3DDRAM，这个数字会急剧上升。这就是希望。
(1:37:46)
But right now, everyone's roadmap is sort of like you go from current, it's called a 6F cell to a 4F cell, and then finally 3DDRAM, like by the end of the decade or early next decade. So there's still like a lot of R&D and manufacturing and integration to be done. I wouldn't call that out of the cards. I think it's very much likely going to happen. It also is going to require a huge retooling of fabs, right? The breakdown of tools in a fab are very different, right? Actually, the lithography tool is the only thing that isn't like that different, but the number of them relative to different types of chemical vapor deposition or atomic layer deposition or dry etch or different kinds of etch chambers with different chemistries,
但现在，每个人的规划都是从当前的，所谓的 6F 单元到 4F 单元，然后最终到 3DDRAM，大概在这个十年末或下一个十年初。所以仍然需要大量的研发、制造和集成工作。我不会说这不可能。我认为这很可能会发生。这也需要对晶圆厂进行大规模的改造，对吧？晶圆厂中工具的配置非常不同，对吧？实际上，光刻工具是唯一没有太大区别的东西，但是相对于不同类型的化学气相沉积或原子层沉积或干法刻蚀或具有不同化学性质的不同类型的刻蚀腔室，
(1:38:26)
all of these things You have all these different kinds of tools for different process nodes. You can't just convert a LogicFab to a DRAMFab or vice versa, back and forth, or a NANDFab to a DRAMFab in a short amount of time. In the same way, existing DRAMFabs We require a lot of retooling just to go from one alpha to one beta to one gamma process nodes, because now they have to add to EUV and change the chemistry stacks for when you're using EUV in terms of deposition and etch, and the EUV tool has to be there. And furthermore, when you change to 3D DRAM, there's going to be an even larger shift. And so there's a lot of retooling of these fabs that needs to happen in terms of the tools.
所有这些东西，针对不同的工艺节点，您需要各种不同的工具。你不能在短时间内将逻辑芯片厂转换为 DRAM 芯片厂，或者反之亦然，也不能将 NAND 芯片厂转换为 DRAM 芯片厂。同样，现有的 DRAM 厂需要大量的改造，才能从一个 Alpha 到一个 Beta 再到一个 Gamma 制程节点，因为现在他们必须增加 EUV，并改变化学堆栈，以便在使用 EUV 时进行沉积和蚀刻，而且 EUV 工具必须到位。此外，当你转向 3D DRAM 时，将会出现更大的转变。因此，就工具而言，这些晶圆厂需要进行大量的改造。

The Skepticism of Space Data Centers
对太空数据中心的怀疑
Dylan says that even if power costs double, you're still at a fraction of the total cost of the GPU. He says that the main challenge is And what we've seen that disperses, right? He says that GPUs are horrendously unreliable. He says that if a GPU has a useful life of five years, and it takes three additional months, probably six, let's say six additional months, then that is 10% of your cluster's useful life.
Dylan 说，即使电力成本翻倍，也只占 GPU 总成本的一小部分。他说，主要的挑战是，我们看到的情况分散了吗？他说，GPU 非常不可靠。他说，如果一个 GPU 的使用寿命是五年，并且需要额外三个月的时间，可能六个月，假设是六个月，那么这将占你集群使用寿命的 10%。
Dylan Patel:
(1:52:59)

The Limitations of Space Data Centers
空间数据中心的局限性
Dylan says that space data centers effectively are not limited by, you know, hey, we have this energy advantage. He says that it's actually just limited by the same contended resource. He says that it doesn't matter if it's on land or in space.
Dylan 说，实际上，空间数据中心不受限于，你知道的，嘿，我们有这种能源优势。他说，它实际上只是受到相同竞争资源的限制。他说，无论是在陆地上还是在太空中，这都无关紧要。
Dylan Patel:
(2:00:30)
A lot of models fit within one scale up domain, but many times you split them across multiple scale up domains. I think that You really have to, as models become more and more sparse, at least this is like the general trend, then you want to ping just a couple experts per GPU. And if leading models today have hundreds, if not thousand experts, then you'd want to run this across hundreds of chips or thousands of chips, even as we continue to advance into the future. And so then you end up with this problem of Well, now you need to connect all these satellites together comms-wise as well.
许多模型都适合在一个扩展域内，但很多时候你会将它们拆分到多个扩展域中。我认为你真的需要，随着模型变得越来越稀疏，至少这是一个总趋势，那么你只想为每个 GPU ping 几个专家。如果当今领先的模型有数百甚至数千个专家，那么你可能希望在数百或数千个芯片上运行它，即使我们不断向未来发展。这样你最终会遇到这个问题，你需要将所有这些卫星通过通信方式连接起来。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(2:01:09)
Okay, so that would be tough. Because I was imagining if there's a world where you could do inference for a batch on a single scale-up, then maybe it's more plausible. But if not, then it's...
好的，那将非常困难。因为我设想，如果存在这样一种情况：你可以在单个扩展上对一批数据进行推理，那么这可能更可行。但如果不是这样，那么...
Dylan Patel:
(2:01:21)
Yeah, I mean, networking these ships together is a problem. And you can't just make the satellite infinitely large, right? A lot of challenges with physics to making a satellite really big, right? So then that's why you need these interconnects between the satellites. Those interconnects are more expensive than the, you know, a cluster like 20% of the cost or 15% of the cost is networking. All of a sudden, now you're making it like space lasers instead of like pretty simple, like lasers that are manufactured in millions of volumes with, you know, pluggable transceivers. And those things are very unreliable as well. More unreliable than the GPUs, by the way, across the life of a cluster, you have to unplug, clean it all the time, right?
是的，将这些设备连接起来是个问题。而且你不能把卫星做得无限大，对吧？在物理学上，制造一个非常大的卫星有很多挑战，对吧？所以你才需要卫星之间的互连。这些互连比集群更昂贵，比如 20% 或 15% 的成本是网络。突然之间，你开始制造太空激光器，而不是制造简单、批量生产的激光器，它们带有可插拔的收发器。而且这些东西也非常不可靠。顺便说一句，在集群的整个生命周期中，它们比 GPU 更不可靠，你必须一直拔掉、清洁它们，对吧？
(2:01:57)
Unplug, replug it just for random reasons. These things are just not as reliable. So you've got that also, that problem as well. Like you've got a more expensive, complicated space laser to communicate instead of this pluggable optical transceiver that's been in super high volume.
仅仅因为一些随机原因，就拔掉、重新插上。这些东西就是没那么可靠。所以你也有这个问题。比如，你需要一个更昂贵、更复杂的太空激光器来进行通信，而不是大量生产的可插拔光收发器。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(2:02:10)
Okay, so all in all, what does that imply for space data centers?
好的，总而言之，这对太空数据中心意味着什么？
Dylan Patel:
(2:02:13)
So space data centers effectively are not limited by, you know, hey, we have this energy advantage. It's actually just limited by the same contended resource. We can only make 200 gigawatts of chips a year by the end of the decade. So what are we going to do to get that capacity? It doesn't matter if it's on land or in space. It doesn't really matter because you can build that power. I think human capabilities and capacity could get to the period where we're adding a terawatt a year globally of various types of power. At some point, we do cross the chasm where space data centers make sense, but it's not this decade.
因此，太空数据中心实际上不受 “嘿，我们有能源优势” 的限制。它实际上只是受到相同竞争资源的限制。到本十年末，我们每年只能制造 200 吉瓦的芯片。那么我们该如何获得这种能力呢？无论它在陆地上还是在太空中，都无关紧要。这真的无关紧要，因为你可以建设电力。我认为人类的能力和产能可以达到这样一个阶段：我们在全球范围内每年增加一太瓦的各种类型的电力。在某个时候，我们确实会跨越鸿沟，太空数据中心变得有意义，但不是在这个十年。

The Optimization of Energy Costs
能源成本的优化
Dylan says that space data centers will eventually be a 10x gain, potentially, as Earth's resources get more and more contentious. He says that if you can run a very hot chip because it allows a lot of...
Dylan 说，随着地球资源变得越来越稀缺，空间数据中心最终可能会带来 10 倍的收益。他说，如果你可以运行一个非常热的芯片，因为它允许大量的……
Dylan Patel:
(2:02:52)
It is much further out once you have Energy constraints actually being a big bottleneck once you have space, land permitting be a much bigger bottleneck as it subsumes more and more of the economy. And chips are no longer the bottleneck because chips are the biggest bottleneck. And so you want them deployed working on AI the moment they're done being manufactured. And so there's a lot of things people are doing to increase that speed faster and faster, whether it be modulizing data centers or even modulizing racks where you actually put the chip in We're at the data center, but only the chip and everything else is already wired up and ready to go at the data center.
一旦能源限制真正成为一个巨大的瓶颈，一旦空间、土地许可成为一个更大的瓶颈，因为它会占据越来越多的经济份额，那将会在更远的未来。芯片不再是瓶颈，因为芯片是最大的瓶颈。所以你希望它们在制造完成后立即被部署并用于人工智能。因此，人们正在做很多事情来提高速度，无论是模块化数据中心，还是模块化机架，你可以把芯片放在数据中心里。但只有芯片，其他所有东西都已经连接好，可以在数据中心使用了。
(2:03:28)
So there's things like this that people are doing to decrease that time that you cannot do in space. (2:06:58)
With Blackwell and VL72, they implemented rack scale up. And that meant all 72 GPUs in the rack could connect to each other at terabytes a second speed. And the speed doubled gen on gen, but also the most important innovation they did was going from eight to 72 in the domain. When we look at Google, their scale-up domain is completely different, right? It has always been on the order of thousands, right? With TPU v4, they had pods the size of 4,000 chips. With v8, they have pods, or v7, they have pods in the 7,000, or sorry, 8,000, 9,000 range. And what's relevant here is that it's not the same as Nvidia. It's not like for like. Google has a topology that's a torus, right?
借助 Blackwell 和 VL72，他们实现了机架规模的 scale up。这意味着机架中的所有 72 个 GPU 都可以以每秒太字节的速度相互连接。速度每一代都翻了一番，但他们做的最重要的创新是从 8 个增加到 72 个。当我们看谷歌时，他们的 scale-up 领域是完全不同的，对吧？它一直是在数千个的量级上，对吧？借助 TPU v4，他们的 pods 大小为 4,000 个芯片。借助 v8，他们有 pods，或者 v7，他们的 pods 在 7,000，或者抱歉，8,000，9,000 范围内。这里相关的是，它与 Nvidia 不同。这不一样。谷歌的拓扑结构是一个环面，对吧？
(2:07:37)
So every chip connects to six neighbors. Rather than Nvidia, the 72 GPUs connect all to all, right? So they can send terabytes a second to each other, to any arbitrary other chip in that pod of scale up. Whereas Google, you have to bounce through chips, right? So this means if TPU-1 needs to talk to TPU-76, then it has to bounce through various chips. And there is always some blocking of resources when you do that. So because that one TPU is only connected to six other TPUs. And so there's a difference in topology and bandwidth and there are trade-offs and advantages of both, right? Google gets to have a massive scale-up domain.
因此，每个芯片都连接到六个邻居。而不是 Nvidia，72 个 GPU 全部连接到所有 GPU，对吧？因此，他们可以以每秒太字节的速度将数据发送到该 scale up pod 中的任何其他任意芯片。而对于谷歌，你必须通过芯片进行反弹，对吧？这意味着如果 TPU-1 需要与 TPU-76 通信，那么它必须通过各种芯片进行反弹。当你这样做时，总会存在一些资源阻塞。因为那个 TPU 只连接到其他六个 TPU。因此，拓扑结构和带宽存在差异，并且两者都有权衡和优势，对吧？谷歌可以拥有大规模的 scale-up 领域。
(2:08:11)
But then they have the trade-off of you have to bounce across chips to get from one chip to another. You can only talk to six direct neighbors. And so there is like this trade-off. And Amazon, it has mutated their scale-up domain. They're somewhere in between Nvidia and Google effectively, where they're trying to make larger scale-up domains. They try and do all-to-all to some extent, which is what with switches, which is what Nvidia does. But also to some extent, they use tourist topologies like Google does. And as we as we advance forward to next generations, all three of them are moving more and more towards a dragonfly topology,
但是，他们必须权衡的是，你必须跨芯片进行反弹才能从一个芯片到达另一个芯片。你只能与六个直接邻居交谈。因此，存在这种权衡。亚马逊已经改变了他们的 scale-up 领域。实际上，它们介于 Nvidia 和谷歌之间，它们正试图建立更大的 scale-up 领域。它们在某种程度上尝试进行全互联，这正是 Nvidia 使用交换机所做的事情。但在某种程度上，他们也像谷歌一样使用环面拓扑。随着我们向下一代发展，它们三个都在越来越多地转向蜻蜓拓扑，
(2:08:44)
which means there's sort of like there is some fully connected elements and there's some elements that are not fully connected. So you can get the scale up to be hundreds or thousands of chips, but also have it not contend for resources when you're bouncing through chips.
这意味着某种程度上存在一些完全连接的元素，并且存在一些未完全连接的元素。因此，你可以将 scale up 扩展到数百或数千个芯片，而且当你通过芯片进行反弹时，它也不会争用资源。

Parameter Scaling and the Allocation of Compute
参数缩放和计算分配
Dwarkesh says that the reason that parameter scaling has been slow and only now are we getting bigger and bigger models from OpenAI and Anthropic is that So original GPT-4 is over a trillion parameters and only now are models starting to approach that again. Dwarkesh 说，参数缩放一直很慢，直到现在我们才从 OpenAI 和 Anthropic 获得越来越大的模型，原因是最初的 GPT-4 超过了 1 万亿个参数，而现在模型才开始再次接近这个数量级。Dylan 说，你从研究中获得的计算效率提升是如此之大，以至于你实际上希望你的大部分计算都用于研究，而不是用于开发。

Well, the model, the compute efficiency gains you get from research are so large, you actually want most of your compute to go to research, not to development. And at least what we've seen empirically is like model cost gets 10x cheaper every year or even more than that. Which at the same scale gets 10x cheaper or to get to reach new frontiers, it costs the same amount or more, right? So you don't want to allocate too many resources to pre-training and RL.
实际上，从研究中获得的计算效率提升非常大，所以你实际上希望将大部分计算资源投入到研究中，而不是开发。因为，你知道，所有这些研究人员都在产生新的想法，尝试它们，测试它们，并继续沿着这条路前进，并进一步推动帕累托最优缩放定律曲线。至少我们凭经验看到的是，模型成本每年降低 10 倍，甚至更多。在相同的规模下，成本降低 10 倍，或者要达到新的前沿，成本相同甚至更高，对吧？所以你不想将太多的资源分配给预训练和强化学习。
(2:11:33)
You actually want to allocate most of your resources to research. And then in the middle is this sort of this like development type period. If you pre-train a 5 trillion parameter model, Now, you have to spend all this time. How many rollouts do you have to do in these RLs? And these rollouts for a trillion parameter model versus a five trillion parameter model are five times larger, which then means it takes, if you wanted to do as many rollouts, maybe the larger model is more sample efficient. Let's say it's 2x more sample efficient. Okay, great. Now you need 2.5x much time of RL to get the model smarter.
你实际上想将大部分资源分配给研究。然后在中间是这种开发类型的时期。如果你预训练一个 5 万亿参数的模型，现在，你必须花费所有的时间。你必须在这些强化学习中进行多少次推出？万亿参数模型和五万亿参数模型的这些推出次数相差五倍，这意味着，如果你想做同样多的推出，也许更大的模型更具有样本效率。假设它的样本效率高出 2 倍。好的，很好。现在你需要 2.5 倍的强化学习时间才能让模型更智能。
(2:12:05)
Or you could RL the smaller model for 2x the time and you'd still have a 25% difference in the big model, which is 2x more sample efficient and doing x number of rollouts versus the small model, which is a trillion parameters, although it's less sample efficient, is doing twice as many rollouts. It's still done faster. And so you get the model faster, sooner, and you've done more RL. And then you can take that model to help you build the next models, help your engineers train and do all these research ideas. And so this feedback loop is actually weighed towards smaller models in every case, no matter what your hardware is.
或者你可以用 2 倍的时间对较小的模型进行强化学习，但大型模型仍然存在 25% 的差异，这意味着大型模型的样本效率是小型模型的 2 倍，且大型模型执行了 x 次 rollout，而小型模型。拥有万亿参数（虽然样本效率较低），但执行的 rollout 次数是前者的两倍。速度仍然更快。因此，你能更快、更早地得到模型，并完成更多的 RL。然后，你可以利用该模型来帮助你构建下一个模型，帮助你的工程师进行训练，并实现所有这些研究想法。因此，无论你的硬件如何，这种反馈循环实际上在所有情况下都倾向于更小的模型。
(2:12:40)
And then as you look to Google, Google does deploy the largest production model of any of the major labs, right, with Gemini Pro. It is a larger model than GPT 5.4. It's a larger model than Opus. And so you end up with, yes, Google does this because they have a unipolar set of compute, right, almost all TPU. Whereas Anthropic is dealing with H100s, H200s, Blackwell, Traniums, TPUs of various generations, right? And OpenAI is dealing with mostly Nvidia right now, but going towards having AMD and Tranium as well. The fleets of compute like Google can just optimize around a larger model and they can leverage a thousand chips in a scale-up domain to get the RL speed much faster.
然后，当你看到谷歌时，谷歌确实部署了所有主要实验室中最大的生产模型，对吧，也就是 Gemini Pro。它的模型比 GPT 5.4 更大，也比 Opus 更大。因此，最终你会发现，没错，谷歌这样做是因为他们拥有一套单极计算能力，对吧，几乎全部是 TPU。而 Anthropic 正在处理 H100、H200、Blackwell、Tranium 以及各种代的 TPU，对吧？OpenAI 目前主要与英伟达合作，但也在朝着 AMD 和 Tranium 方向发展。像谷歌这样的计算集群可以围绕更大的模型进行优化，并且他们可以在纵向扩展领域利用数千个芯片，从而大大提高 RL 速度。
(2:13:30)
So that you can actually have this feedback loop be fast. But at the end of the day, in isolation, you almost always want to go with a smaller model that gets RL'd faster and gets deployed into research and development. So you can build the next thing and get more compute efficiency wins. And then this compounding effect of, oh, I made a smaller model that I RL'd more, that I then deployed into research and development earlier. And I spent less compute on the training itself because I was able to allocate more compute to the research. This like compounding effect of being able to do the research faster and faster and faster is potentially a faster takeoff.
这样你才能真正让这个反馈循环变得快速。但归根结底，在孤立的情况下，你几乎总是希望使用更小的模型，以便更快地进行 RL，并将其部署到研发中。这样你就能构建下一个产品，并在计算效率方面取得更多胜利。然后就会产生这种复合效应，哦，我做了一个更小的模型，我对其进行了更多的 RL，然后我更早地将其部署到研发中。而且我减少了训练本身的计算量，因为我能够分配更多的计算资源给研究。这种能够更快地进行研究的复合效应，有可能实现更快的起飞。
(2:14:02)
And that's all these companies want is fastest takeoff possible.
而这正是所有公司想要的，尽可能快的起飞。

The Use of Spreadsheets and the Belief in AGI
电子表格的使用和对 AGI 的信念
Dwarkesh asks why is Leopold the only person that is using your spreadsheets to make outrageous money. 台积电和苹果的出局

Dylan says that the challenge of this is chip design timelines take a long while. He says that TSMC is not going to kick out Apple.
Dwarkesh 问道，如果台积电说，内存逻辑等等，N3 主要用于人工智能加速器，但接下来是 N2，它现在主要用于苹果，台积电能做到吗。Dylan 说，这里的挑战是芯片设计时间线很长。他说，台积电不会把苹果踢出去。
Dwarkesh Patel:
(2:18:25)
Okay, maybe some rapid fire to close out. Can TSMC, if you're saying, look, the memory logic, et cetera, the N3 is mostly going to be AI accelerators, but then there's N2, which is mostly Apple now. And then in the future, I guess AI would also want to go on N2. Can Can they kick out Apple if Nvidia and Amazon and Google say, hey, we're willing to pay a lot of money for N2 capacity?
好的，也许可以快速结束。如果你说，TSMC，内存逻辑等等，N3 主要用于 AI 加速器，但是 N2 主要用于苹果。然后在未来，我想 AI 也想使用 N2。如果英伟达、亚马逊和谷歌说，嘿，我们愿意为 N2 产能支付很多钱，他们能踢掉苹果吗？
Dylan Patel:
(2:18:58)
So I think the challenge of this is chip design timelines take a long while. And so that's more than a year. And the designs that are on two nanometer are more than a year out. And so what would really happen is Apple or sorry, Nvidia and all these others will be like, hey, we're going to prepay for the capacity and you're going to expand it for us. And then Apple will be, and maybe TSMC takes a little bit of margin, but not a ton. They're not going to kick Apple out entirely, right? What they're going to do is when Apple orders X, they may say, hey, we project you only need Y or X minus one. And so that's what we're going to give you is X minus one.
所以我认为这里的挑战是芯片设计的时间线很长。这需要一年多的时间。而两纳米的设计需要一年多的时间才能完成。所以真正会发生的是苹果，或者抱歉，英伟达和所有其他人会说，嘿，我们将预先支付产能，你将为我们扩大产能。然后苹果会......也许 TSMC 会获得一点利润，但不会太多。他们不会完全踢掉苹果，对吧？他们要做的是，当苹果订购 X 时，他们可能会说，嘿，我们预计你只需要 Y 或 X 减 1。所以我们要给你的是 X 减 1。
(2:19:30)
And then that flex capacity Apple's kind of screwed on. Whereas traditionally Apple's always overordered by like 10% and cut back by 10% over the course of the year. And some years they hit the entire 10%, just, you know, volumes vary, right? Based on the season and macro, blah, blah, blah, blah, blah. And so I don't think TSMC would kick out Apple. I think Apple will become a smaller and smaller and smaller percentage of TSMC's revenue and therefore be less relevant for TSMC to cater to their demands. And TSMC could eventually start saying, hey, you've got to pre-book your capacity for next year, for two years out, and you have to pre-pay for the CapEx because that's what Nvidia and Amazon and Google are doing.
然后苹果在灵活产能方面有点倒霉。而传统上，苹果总是超额订购 10%，并在一年内削减 10%。有些年份他们达到了整个 10%，只是，你知道，销量会有所不同，对吧？基于季节和宏观，等等，等等，等等。所以我不认为 TSMC 会踢掉苹果。我认为苹果在 TSMC 收入中所占的比例会越来越小，因此 TSMC 满足他们的需求也变得越来越不重要。TSMC 最终可能会开始说，嘿，你必须预订明年，甚至两年后的产能，而且你必须预先支付资本支出，因为英伟达、亚马逊和谷歌都在这样做。

Humanoids and the Centralization of Intelligence
类人机器人和智能的集中化
Dwarkesh asks if humanoids take off faster than people expect, if by 2030 there's millions of humanoids running around, which each need local compute, Any thoughts on what that implies. Dylan says that to some extent, you don't need to have all the intelligence in the robot. He says that in the future, even with robots that are out physically in the world, I mean, obviously, knowledge work will be done in a centralized way from data centers with hundreds of thousands of instances or maybe millions of instances.

The Slowing of US and Global GDP
美国和全球 GDP 的放缓
Dylan says that if you ship out all the process engineers and assuming it's like hot enough that you destroy the fabs, no one has all the fabs in Taiwan now. He says that you've drastically slowed US and global GDP, not just growth, you've shrank the GDP massively.
Dylan 说，如果你运走了所有的工艺工程师，并假设情况非常紧急，以至于你摧毁了晶圆厂，现在没有人拥有台湾所有的晶圆厂。他说，你已经大大减缓了美国和全球的 GDP，不仅仅是增长，你已经大幅度地缩小了 GDP。
Dylan Patel:
(2:29:04)
If you ship out all the process engineers and assuming it's like hot enough that you destroy the fabs, no one has all the fabs in Taiwan now. Which is a big risk, right? These tools actually use a lot of semiconductors which are manufactured in Taiwan. It's like a snake eating its own tail sort of like meme because you can't make the tools without the chips from Taiwan which you can't use without the tools in Taiwan. There's obviously some diversification there but And they don't use super advanced chips in lithography tools, but at the end of the day, there is some tail eating the dragon.
如果你运走所有的工艺工程师，并假设情况足够糟糕，你摧毁了晶圆厂，现在没有人拥有台湾所有的晶圆厂。这是一个很大的风险，对吧？这些工具实际上使用了大量在台湾制造的半导体。这就像一条蛇在吃自己的尾巴，因为没有台湾的芯片就无法制造工具，而没有台湾的工具就无法使用芯片。显然存在一些多元化，而且他们在光刻工具中没有使用超级先进的芯片，但最终，还是有点像尾巴在吃龙。
(2:29:36)
Just shipping out all the engineers and blowing up the fabs means China has a stronger semiconductor supply chain than the rest of the world, right? In terms of verticalization, now that you've removed Taiwan, and now you've got all the know-how, but you've got to replicate it in, let's say, Arizona or wherever for TSMC. And it's going to take a long time to build all the capacity that TSMC has had built over the years. And so you've drastically slowed US and global GDP, not just growth, you've shrank the GDP massively. And you've got a lot bigger problems. And your incremental ability to add compute goes to almost zero, right? Instead of hundreds of gigawatts a year by the end of decade, let's say by the end of the decade,
仅仅运走所有的工程师并炸毁晶圆厂，意味着中国拥有比世界其他地区更强大的半导体供应链，对吧？就垂直整合而言，既然你已经移除了台湾，现在你拥有了所有的技术，但你必须在亚利桑那州或台积电的任何地方复制它。而且要建立起台积电多年来积累的所有产能，需要很长时间。因此，你已经大大减缓了美国和全球的 GDP，不仅仅是增长，你已经大规模地缩减了 GDP。而且你还有更大的问题。而且你增加计算能力的增量能力几乎为零，对吧？假设到本十年末，原本可以达到每年数百吉瓦，
(2:30:19)
something happens to Taiwan. Now you're at maybe like 10 gigawatts across Intel and Samsung or 20 gigawatts. It's like nothing. But now all of a sudden you've like really caused some crazy dynamics in AI. Of course you have all the existing capacity, but that existing capacity pales in comparison to the capacity that's being expanded.
如果台湾发生什么事。现在你可能只有英特尔和三星的 10 吉瓦或 20 吉瓦。几乎什么都不是。但现在你突然在 AI 领域造成了一些疯狂的动态。当然，你拥有所有现有的产能，但现有的产能与正在扩大的产能相比相形见绌。
